<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of <i>30 Rock</i> characters</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(February 2013)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>

</table>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/30_Rock" title="30 Rock">30 Rock</a></i> is an American <a href="/wiki/Television_comedy" title="Television comedy">television comedy</a> <a href="/wiki/Television_program" title="Television program">series</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Tina_Fey" title="Tina Fey">Tina Fey</a> which airs on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>. The series takes place behind the scenes of a fictional <a href="/wiki/Live_television" title="Live television">live</a> <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">sketch comedy</a> series, also airing on NBC; the name "30 Rock" refers to the address of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GE_Building" title="GE Building">GE Building</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBC_Studios_(New_York)" title="NBC Studios (New York)">NBC Studios</a> is located (30 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Plaza" title="Rockefeller Plaza">Rockefeller Plaza</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The series has an <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a> consisting of 14 regular cast members: <a href="/wiki/Tina_Fey" title="Tina Fey">Tina Fey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alec_Baldwin" title="Alec Baldwin">Alec Baldwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan" title="Tracy Morgan">Tracy Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Krakowski" title="Jane Krakowski">Jane Krakowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_McBrayer" title="Jack McBrayer">Jack McBrayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Adsit" title="Scott Adsit">Scott Adsit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judah_Friedlander" title="Judah Friedlander">Judah Friedlander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katrina_Bowden" title="Katrina Bowden">Katrina Bowden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Powell" title="Keith Powell">Keith Powell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lonny_Ross" title="Lonny Ross">Lonny Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Lutz" title="John Lutz">John Lutz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Brown_(actor)" title="Kevin Brown (actor)">Kevin Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grizz_Chapman" title="Grizz Chapman">Grizz Chapman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maulik_Pancholy" title="Maulik Pancholy">Maulik Pancholy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbcseriespress_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbcseriespress-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_characters">Main characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Main characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The series features seven characters appearing during the <a href="/wiki/Opening_credits" title="Opening credits">opening credits</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liz_Lemon" title="Liz Lemon">Liz Lemon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jenna_Maroney" title="Jenna Maroney">Jenna Maroney</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liz_Lemon">Liz Lemon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Liz Lemon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liz_Lemon" title="Liz Lemon">Liz Lemon</a></div>
<p><b>Elizabeth Miervaldis "Liz" Lemon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tina_Fey" title="Tina Fey">Tina Fey</a>), the series' protagonist, is <a href="/wiki/Head_writer" title="Head writer">head writer</a> of <i>TGS with Tracy Jordan</i>. Jack Donaghy calls her a "New York third-wave feminist, college-educated, single-and-pretending-to-be-happy-about-it, over-scheduled, undersexed, you buy any magazine that says 'healthy body image' on the cover and every two years you take up knitting for... a week." Lemon is a <i>Star Wars</i> fan and is portrayed as a "geek." She also lacks certain social skills and is a stress eater, particularly ingesting junk food. She is generally shown to have liberal political views. Despite her high standards in men, personified in her imaginary perfect husband, <a href="#Astronaut_Mike_Dexter">Astronaut Mike Dexter</a>, Lemon has had some "really terrible boyfriends," but eventually finds happiness with Criss Chross, with whom she adopts two children.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jack_Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Jack Donaghy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jack_Donaghy" title="Jack Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</a></div>
<p><b>John Francis "Jack" Donaghy</b> (<a href="/wiki/Alec_Baldwin" title="Alec Baldwin">Alec Baldwin</a>) is the decisive, controlling, suave network executive who must deal with (and/or causes) unusual events at <i>TGS</i>. He is an Irish-American Catholic and a <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>. Donaghy is portrayed as a slick, brilliant and scrupulous network executive who directs many overtly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Backhanded_compliment" title="Backhanded compliment">backhanded compliments</a> to Liz. Lemon (as he refers to her) and Donaghy have a <a href="/wiki/Work_spouse" title="Work spouse">work spouse</a> relationship. Jack was married two times (and engaged two other times), and with his second wife, television reporter Avery Jessup, he has a daughter, Liddy Elizabeth Donaghy, named after Liz Lemon. Avery and Jack were divorced after her return from North Korea (where she was held hostage by Kim Jong Il) when they admit they only married because of Avery's pregnancy. Shortly after becoming the CEO of Kabletown, Jack suffered an emotional crisis and resigned, only to return to General Electric.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tracy_Jordan">Tracy Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tracy Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Jordan" title="Tracy Jordan">Tracy Jordan</a></div>
<p><b>Tracy Jordan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan" title="Tracy Morgan">Tracy Morgan</a>) is the loose-cannon star of <i>TGS.</i> He is a <a href="/wiki/Movie_star" title="Movie star">movie star</a> with a reputation for erratic behavior. This reputation is well-deserved; much of it is an intentional attempt on his part to maintain his "crazy" persona in the eyes of the media. In <a href="/wiki/Pilot_(30_Rock)" title="Pilot (30 Rock)">the pilot episode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Donaghy" title="Jack Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</a> forces <a href="/wiki/Liz_Lemon" title="Liz Lemon">Liz Lemon</a> to hire Tracy as the new star of her <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">sketch comedy</a> program <i>The Girlie Show.</i> To the chagrin of Liz and Jenna, Jack renames the show <i>TGS with Tracy Jordan</i> in the following episode. Tracy has remained the star of <i>TGS</i> ever since.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jenna_Maroney">Jenna Maroney</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jenna Maroney">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jenna_Maroney" title="Jenna Maroney">Jenna Maroney</a></div>
<p><b>Jenna Maroney</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jane_Krakowski" title="Jane Krakowski">Jane Krakowski</a>) is the histrionic costar of <i>TGS</i>, and Liz's best friend. She is often shown as being extremely insecure about herself. A recurring <a href="/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)" title="Motif (visual arts)">motif</a> in the show is Jenna's pursuit of fame through some ill-advised project ending up in public humiliation from which she never learns. She is, in other words, a typical <a href="/wiki/Prima_donna" title="Prima donna">prima donna</a>. Off-camera she is comically conceited, frequently lying about her age and using her sexuality to manipulate men (almost always to bad effect).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenneth_Parcell">Kenneth Parcell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Kenneth Parcell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Parcell" title="Kenneth Parcell">Kenneth Parcell</a></div>
<p><b>Kenneth Ellen Parcell</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jack_McBrayer" title="Jack McBrayer">Jack McBrayer</a>) is a cheerful, obedient <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern</a>-born <a href="/wiki/NBC_page" title="NBC page">NBC page</a> who "lives for television". In the early episodes, Kenneth seemed unfamiliar with some of Liz's staff (and Liz herself). In the pilot, Liz refers to Kenneth as "that NBC page". As the series progressed, his character became familiar with the other staff of <i>TGS</i> (including Jack Donaghy). Kenneth acts as Tracy Jordan's personal assistant (for instance, getting Tracy <a href="/wiki/Nachos" title="Nachos">nachos</a> from <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>); he is a member of Tracy's entourage and becomes close to Tracy, Grizz, and Dot Com. By the end of the series, he ends up as the president of NBC.</p>
<p>It is revealed several times over the course of the show that not only may Kenneth not sleep, be immortal, and possibly be a clones, but also as stated by his mother (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_O%27Hara" title="Catherine O'Hara">Catherine O'Hara</a>) that at the time of his birth he said to her, "Mama, I am not a person. My body is just a flesh vessel for an immortal being whose name, if you heard it, would make you lose your mind."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pete_Hornberger">Pete Hornberger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pete Hornberger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ScottAdsit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="960" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/ScottAdsit.jpg/170px-ScottAdsit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/ScottAdsit.jpg/255px-ScottAdsit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/ScottAdsit.jpg/340px-ScottAdsit.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ScottAdsit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Scott Adsit portrays Pete Hornberger</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Peter "Pete" Hornberger</b> (<a href="/wiki/Scott_Adsit" title="Scott Adsit">Scott Adsit</a>) is one of the producers of <i>TGS</i>, who often serves as a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Straight_man" title="wiktionary:Straight man">straight man</a> to the other characters. As the show goes on he slowly descends into a pathetic state of insanity. He works closely with and serves as a trusted friend to Liz, whom, as stated in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blind_Date_(30_Rock_episode)" title="Blind Date (30 Rock episode)">Blind Date</a>", he has known for ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blind_Date_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blind_Date-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early seasons, Pete is Liz's closest friend at work and the only one she can rely on. Much like Liz, Pete generally plays straight man to the other characters, especially to Liz when she is temporarily pushed over the edge. Prior to his work on TGS, Pete was a skilled archer qualified to compete in the 1980 Summer Olympics, but did not get to go when President Carter decided to boycott the Moscow games. Later episode stated he was a member of the band <a href="/wiki/Loverboy" title="Loverboy">Loverboy</a> during his teenage years and that his father was a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>.</p>
<p>Pete is married and he has four sons and a daughter. Aside from a brief scene in the pilot where Pete appears at home with one of his sons, the members of his family were unseen characters until the episode "Greenzo". In one episode, Pete reveals that he is afraid of his son Kyle, who is apparently very strong and, in "Black Tie," he spoke with his son Kaleb over the telephone, pretending to be Elmo, in order to encourage his son to "aim your pee-pee at the potty." In "Greenzo", Liz mentions he has three sons named Robert and Jack, and an unnamed one referred to as "that creepy little one who's always rubbing himself on the carpet". In the episode "Anna Howard Shaw Day", his daughter Evelyn is selling cookies for a school fundraiser. His wife Paula is implied to have a rather overbearing personality and Pete often goes to great lengths to make her happy, as in "Up All Night" when he realized that it was Valentine's Day, which also happens to be his wife's birthday. Pete also passed when one of Tracy's entourage expressed interest in him during that episode, showing that he may not always be happy in his marriage but he remains faithful. In the episode "Tracy Does Conan," Pete stated that his wife wishes he was not bald and, in "Black Tie," Pete mentions that they were married in a botanical garden. He lied to his wife about getting a vasectomy, but, as of "The Fighting Irish," she's getting suspicious. Therefore, Pete has asked Liz for the keys to her apartment for "my own safety." He is still living with Liz as of "Greenzo." However, Liz finds out that Pete and Paula are having an "affair" where they sneak around and use her apartment for trysts that include silk scarves and Pop-Tarts; Pete tells her that he and his wife got pregnant almost immediately after they began dating and have never had an exciting romantic/sexual life because of that, so they have found this way to spark their marriage.</p>
<p>With his role of Liz's confidant increasingly filled by Jack Donaghy, Pete played increasingly reduced roles as the series continued, although his marital woes and inability to catch a break were increasingly mined for humor. Jack pities Pete for his aimlessness and unattractive appearance, and occasionally attempts to boost his confidence, beginning by convincing him to wear a wig for a week in "<a href="/wiki/Tracy_Does_Conan" title="Tracy Does Conan">Tracy Does Conan</a>." In "<a href="/wiki/Nothing_Left_to_Lose" title="Nothing Left to Lose">Nothing Left to Lose</a>", Jack is shocked to find out that Pete's only ambition is to remain in his current job. Jack attempts to help Pete by having him make adjustments to his lifestyle, including shaving off what remains of his hair. Unfortunately, it is revealed that his ring of hair was hiding an obscene birthmark that Jack describes as "a swastika made of penises", leading him to be beaten in the street and forced to wear another wig.</p>
<p>When TGS is canceled in <a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>, Pete implies repeatedly he is planning to fake his death and escape from his life and family. He succeeds in doing so, setting up a new identity under the name "Dan Silversmith" in <a href="/wiki/Hickory,_North_Carolina" title="Hickory, North Carolina">Hickory, North Carolina</a>, but is tracked down a year later by his wife Paula and meekly returns to his previous existence.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frank_Rossitano">Frank Rossitano</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Frank Rossitano">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg/170px-10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg/255px-10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg/340px-10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10.9.10JudahFriedlanderByLuigiNovi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Judah Friedlander portrays Frank Rossitano</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Francis "Frank" Rossitano</b> (<a href="/wiki/Judah_Friedlander" title="Judah Friedlander">Judah Friedlander</a>; <a href="/wiki/Fred_Armisen" title="Fred Armisen">Fred Armisen</a> in select scenes of "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>") is a writer at TGS of Sicilian descent. After Liz, Frank is the most prominently-featured and prolific writer of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Show-within-a-show" title="Show-within-a-show">show-within-a-show</a>. Frank is habitually slovenly and childish; he lives with his mother and is an aficionado of video games, comic books and figurines, and pornography. He wears a variety of <a href="/wiki/Trucker_hat" title="Trucker hat">trucker hats</a> with humorous phrases (which Friedlander also wears in real life) and large, thick-lensed glasses. Frank delivers most lines in a deadpan style, and is often shown to be something of a perverse character with an obvious interest in the opposite gender (although in one episode Frank questions his sexuality after meeting a physically attractive man named Jamie), Frank appears to have an understanding of popular culture and sometimes displays surprising amounts of intelligence. Frank is <a href="/wiki/Peanut_allergy" title="Peanut allergy">allergic to peanuts</a>. In "<a href="/wiki/Audition_Day" title="Audition Day">Audition Day</a>" it is revealed that he is a standup comedian.</p>
<p>Friedlander says he makes the hats for his character himself, using phrases he invents;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> in episode S03E18 where Liz is forced to stay home, one of her final requests before being forced out of the building was to know what Frank's hat said. Frank first started wearing the hats at age 14; his eighth-grade class photo shows him in a hat reading "My First Hat".</p>
<p>Frank was raised largely by his mother Sylvia after his father, a lawyer for the mafia, went into the Witness Protection Program. Sylvia's fear for her son led him to leave law school at her insistence and enter comedy. In "<a href="/wiki/Goodbye,_My_Friend" title="Goodbye, My Friend">Goodbye, My Friend</a>," Jack Donaghy learns of Frank's legal aspirations and offers him a scholarship to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_University_Law_School" title="Columbia University Law School">Columbia University Law School</a>, but reneges on his offer after Sylvia warns him of the danger in which a law career would place Frank due to his family's mafia connections. Frank pursues women frequently, usually older, psychologically damaged, or physically unattractive women he considers "low-hanging fruit". Though it is hinted in the episode "Jackie Jormp Jomp" that him and Cerie have a secret relationship. The great love of Frank's life occurred at the age of 14, where he had an affair with his middle-school teacher, Lynn Onkmann. She was sent to prison for the offense, but he remained in love with her and after her release in the 5th Season of 30 Rock, they reconciled and began a relationship over the objections of pretty much everyone else.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cerie">Cerie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cerie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1760" data-file-width="1251" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg/170px-Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg/255px-Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg/340px-Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_Bowden_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Katrina Bowden portrays Cerie</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Cerie Xerox</b> (<a href="/wiki/Katrina_Bowden" title="Katrina Bowden">Katrina Bowden</a>) is Liz's young, pretty, laid-back assistant. She is an object of intense sexual desire for the male writers of <i>TGS</i> because of her beauty and very revealing clothing. However, she seems to be unaware of the effect she has on men, believing that the reason Liz does not approve of the way she dresses is because Liz has "one of those body image things". She frequently receives drunken phone sex messages, and she states that she does not think that they are cute, even when they are from Liz.</p>
<p>In "<a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Writer" title="Jack the Writer">Jack the Writer</a>", she tells Liz that her goal in life is to "marry rich and then design handbags." She seems to be very successful because of her charm and good looks and is the object of insults from insecure women. Despite her appearance and unawareness, Cerie has proved herself to be intelligent on multiple occasions, usually with ironic comedy.</p>
<p>In "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>", Cerie becomes engaged to a wealthy man named Aris, after dating him for five weeks. When Liz tells Cerie that she may be rushing into marriage, Cerie replies that she would only be able to be a "young hot mom" for a limited time, and that she didn't want to be "like... 50" when her children graduate from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a>. If their first child is a girl, possible names include "Bookcase", "Sandstorm", and "Hat", though Cerie thinks "Hat" is "more of a boy's name". In "<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>," she stated that she and Aris were fighting because he wants a <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a> wedding and she disagrees with the Church's <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">stance on Cyprus</a>; soon after, he is kidnapped by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_pirates" title="Somali pirates">Somali pirates</a>. Cerie and Aris finally marry three seasons later in "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", with Liz and the Somali pirates as members of the wedding party.</p>
<p>In "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Santa_(30_Rock)" title="Secret Santa (30 Rock)">Secret Santa</a>", Cerie tells Jack Donaghy and Liz Lemon that her mother was born in 1976. This probably means that Cerie's mother was a teen mom when Cerie was born. However, in a previous episode, Cerie said that her mother is 38 years old.</p>
<p>Cerie states in "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>" that she quit years earlier, but inexplicably kept coming to work. She joins the rest of the <i>TGS</i> crew and cast on-stage, to resign personally to the Kabletown board of directors, in order to prevent the show from being re-commissioned and thus enable Liz to devote her time to her newly adopted children. She sticks around to pack up the <i>TGS</i> writers' room, and orders both the writers' would-be last lunch which Liz dictates, and its replacement decreed by Lutz. ("<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>")</p>
<p>Jenna is intimidated by Cerie's youth. When seeing Cerie propping her feet up on her desk without her shoes in "<a href="/wiki/Greenzo" title="Greenzo">Greenzo</a>", Jenna assumes bare feet are "in" and pads around shoeless in the hope of appearing young and hip. Immediately upon arriving at <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">LAX</a> to start her post-<i>TGS</i> film career in "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", Jenna sees nothing but beautiful 20-something women and is approached by Cerie's look-alike who addresses her as "Ma'am" and asks if she needs a wheelchair to baggage claim.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toofer_Spurlock">Toofer Spurlock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Toofer Spurlock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>James "Toofer" Spurlock</b> (<a href="/wiki/Keith_Powell" title="Keith Powell">Keith Powell</a>) is a proud <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> alumnus, Harvard <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krokodiloes" title="Krokodiloes">Krokodiloes</a> alumnus, and <i>TGS</i> writer, who often disagrees with Tracy and Frank (although he and Frank often socialize with Lutz). He detests the stereotypical aspects of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_culture" title="African American culture">black culture</a> he believes are embodied by <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Jordan" title="Tracy Jordan">Tracy Jordan</a>, and he serves as a <a href="/wiki/Foil_(literature)" title="Foil (literature)">foil</a> to Tracy. According to Liz, Toofer is "afraid of black people". He claims pride in his black heritage, showing off a photo of an ancestor who was an officer in the Civil War; later, he discovers the man actually fought for the Confederacy. According to Jack, his nickname is "Toofer" because "with him you get a two-for-one; he's a black guy and a <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> guy". Frank (with whom he shares an office) called him a "black nerd" √† la <a href="/wiki/Steve_Urkel" title="Steve Urkel">Steve Urkel</a>. It was revealed in season 4, episode 17 that Toofer was only hired because of <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a>; he quits in anger, before he agrees to return. He insisted that in order to return, his fellow writers must stop calling him Toofer, but relented when they suggested more nicknames. Pete's suggestion of "Threefer, because you're also gay," is the first time that 'Toofers' sexuality is officially called into question, though Liz had previously insulted him, saying "Look, it's Sherlock Homo here to solve the case of the gay sweater." In many episodes, like "The Pilot," "TGS Hates Women," "Anna Howard Shaw Day," and "Up All Night," Toofer has shown an attraction to women. The character was named after series writer <a href="/wiki/Robert_Carlock" title="Robert Carlock">Robert Carlock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grizz">Grizz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grizz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Warren "Grizz" Griswold</b> (<a href="/wiki/Grizz_Chapman" title="Grizz Chapman">Grizz Chapman</a>) is a member of Tracy's entourage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardball_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardball-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seinfeldvision_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-seinfeldvision-7">[7]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Recurring_character" title="Recurring character">recurring character</a> during the first two seasons, he is credited as a series regular in seasons three and four. Within the entourage, Grizz is charged with "sitting on" Tracy when he is overstimulated, in addition to a very fluid list of other responsibilities. In season 1 Grizz was apparently Tracy's financial manager, and in season 5 he was suggested to be Tracy and <a href="/wiki/Adam_West" title="Adam West">Adam West</a>'s talent manager. Despite his calm demeanor, Grizz is shown to be a romantic and deeply emotional man. "Sexual history" between Grizz and Liz Lemon (whom he alone addresses as 'Beth') is referred to in several episodes. The two are seen passionately kissing at Kenneth's party in "<a href="/wiki/Greenzo" title="Greenzo">Greenzo</a>." Despite their history, he cajoles her into serving as his "woman of honor" (i.e., female best man) in his wedding to his fianc√©e, Feyonc√©. In "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>" it is revealed that Tracy and Grizz attended high school together. Grizz is the most physically imposing member of Tracy's entourage and the cast; referencing their long friendship in "<a href="/wiki/Argus_(30_Rock)" title="Argus (30 Rock)">Argus</a>," Tracy tells him "I've known you since you were six feet tall!"</p>
<p>Grizz reads <a href="/wiki/George_R._R._Martin" title="George R. R. Martin">George R. R. Martin</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">A Song of Ice and Fire</a></i> and expressed shock at a climactic moment toward the end of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Game_of_Thrones" title="A Game of Thrones">A Game of Thrones</a></i>.</p>
<p>With the cancellation of <i>TGS</i>, Grizz remains at NBC. He is cast as the lead in a fish-out-of-water situation comedy developed by Dot Com, <i>Grizz &amp; Herz</i>, in which his character runs an inn in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_New_Mexico" title="Santa Fe, New Mexico">Santa Fe</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>. Liz eventually follows the duo, taking a behind-the-camera position and occasionally bringing her adopted children to work. ("<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>")</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dot_Com">Dot Com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Dot Com">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Walter "Dot Com" Slattery</b> (<a href="/wiki/Kevin_Brown_(actor)" title="Kevin Brown (actor)">Kevin Brown</a>) is another member of Tracy's entourage. Another <a href="/wiki/Recurring_character" title="Recurring character">recurring character</a> during the first two seasons, he is also credited as a series regular during seasons three and four. Dot Com is Tracy's driver and cook; in "<a href="/wiki/Hard_Ball" title="Hard Ball">Hard Ball</a>", their last names are revealed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardball_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-hardball-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seinfeldvision_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-seinfeldvision-7">[7]</a></sup> Dot Com is erudite and intellectual; he is a 1993 graduate of <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_University" title="Wesleyan University">Wesleyan University</a>, aspires to screenwriting, and hints at successful entrepreneurial ventures. He credits a former campaign of his for a city council seat as having "raised the level of discourse in this city," even though he lost the election. Dot Com once portrayed Boris Alexeyevich Trigorin in <a href="/wiki/Anton_Chekhov" title="Anton Chekhov">Anton Chekhov</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Seagull" title="The Seagull">The Seagull</a></i>, a role which Tracy praised, saying he saw Walter "become" Trigorin. Dot Com and Grizz are old friends, having met at a "summer camp for giants" ("<a href="/wiki/Argus_(30_Rock)" title="Argus (30 Rock)">Argus</a>"). Like Tracy, Walter grew up in the <a href="/wiki/South_Bronx" title="South Bronx">South Bronx</a>, though without experiencing poverty ("I wanted for nothing as a child, but that brings its own challenges," he notes, with Tracy responding "Shut up, Dot Com!"). Dot Com often serves as the voice of sanity within the series, and finds himself ignored with mounting frustration. During seasons 3 and 4, we learn that he is in love with Grizz's fianc√©e, with whom he is implied to have had an affair.</p>
<p>With the cancellation of <i>TGS</i>, Dot Com develops Grizz's sitcom, <i>Grizz &amp; Herz</i>. He is soon joined behind the camera by Liz Lemon. ("<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>")</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jonathan">Jonathan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Jonathan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maulik_pancholy_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="239" data-file-width="191" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Maulik_pancholy_cropped.jpg/170px-Maulik_pancholy_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Maulik_pancholy_cropped.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maulik_pancholy_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maulik Pancholy portrays Jonathan, Jack's assistant</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Jonathan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Maulik_Pancholy" title="Maulik Pancholy">Maulik Pancholy</a>) is Jack's assistant. Jonathan harbours a desperate crush on Jack. His obsessive admiration of his boss is coupled with disdain towards Liz, whom he considers unworthy of Jack's attention. In the episode "<a href="/wiki/Believe_in_the_Stars" title="Believe in the Stars">Believe in the Stars</a>," Jack reveals he only hired him because he was heavily medicated on Comanaprosil and he mistook Jonathan for <a href="/wiki/M._Night_Shyamalan" title="M. Night Shyamalan">M. Night Shyamalan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In season 4, episode 11 ("<a href="/wiki/Winter_Madness" title="Winter Madness">Winter Madness</a>") it is revealed that Jonathan is of Indian descent, and in episode 18 ("<a href="/wiki/Khonani" title="Khonani">Khonani</a>") he addresses the janitor Khonani in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Hindi" title="Standard Hindi">Hindi</a>. Elsewhere, he mentions meeting his "birth parents," revealing he is adopted, and when in the season-five episode <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Stay_Together_(30_Rock)" title="Let's Stay Together (30 Rock)">Let's Stay Together</a>, when Jack asks Jonathan to provide a distraction by pretending to be a stereotypical Indian and faking an Indian accent, Jonathan objects, "But I'm from <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto</a>!" More than once Jonathan has made racist comments about people from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Kashmir" title="Indian Kashmir">Indian Kashmir</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Khonani" title="Khonani">Khonani</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Righteous_Cowboy_Lightning" title="Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning">Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning</a>").</p>
<p>As a Christmas gift one year, Jack secured the release of Jonathan's sister from a North Korean prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-9">[9]</a></sup> Jack's wife Avery was later kidnapped to North Korea herself. Liz once caught Jonathan wearing a wedding dress and dancing with one of Jack's suits. ("<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>")</p>
<p>Jonathan retains his position when Jack is replaced by Kathy Geiss, and is heartbroken by Jack's departure. He stays on as Jack's assistant when Jack is reinstated and keeps the same office despite his promotion to chairman of NBC. Jack fires Jonathan in "<a href="/wiki/Cutbacks_(30_Rock)" title="Cutbacks (30 Rock)">Cutbacks</a>," but he reappears as Jack's assistant three episodes later without explanation. He relocates with Jack to a suite upstairs when the latter is appointed chairman of Kabletown and eschews the company's Philadelphia headquarters in favour of remaining in the G.E. Building. ("<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>" / "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>")</p>
<p>Jonathan is off-camera throughout the show's sixth season, something that the characters appear not to notice. His disappearance was due to actor Pancholy's costarring role on another NBC sitcom, <i><a href="/wiki/Whitney_(TV_series)" title="Whitney (TV series)">Whitney</a></i>. Pancholy exists within the <i>30 Rock</i> universe independently of Jonathan, being mentioned by Jack in "<a href="/wiki/The_Ballad_of_Kenneth_Parcell" title="The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell">The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell</a>" during that period; Alec Baldwin likewise exists independently of Jack who mentions the actor in "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>". Jonathan returns in season seven, stating that he was away looking after his sick grandmother. ("<a href="/wiki/The_Beginning_of_the_End_(30_Rock)" title="The Beginning of the End (30 Rock)">The Beginning of the End</a>")</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lutz">Lutz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Lutz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lutz,_John_(WGA).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg/170px-Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg/255px-Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg/340px-Lutz%2C_John_%28WGA%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lutz,_John_(WGA).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
John Lutz portrays Lutz</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Johnny "J. D." Lutz</b> (<a href="/wiki/John_Lutz" title="John Lutz">John Lutz</a>) is a lazy, overweight <i>TGS</i> writer who is often ridiculed by the rest of the staff. When characters enter the room they sometimes yell, "Shut up, Lutz!" even if Lutz was not speaking at the time. The other characters are unconcerned about his well-being; when Lutz ran headfirst into a wall in "<a href="/wiki/The_Ones_(30_Rock)" title="The Ones (30 Rock)">The Ones</a>", no one helped him until a wall-mounted television fell on him, and even then, Pete (the producer) tells the writers, who instigated the incident, "I hope you've learned your lesson. Because of what you did, we almost lost a monitor." Lutz is originally from <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> (which he hates), and is part <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>. His first two initials were mentioned in "<a href="/wiki/The_Aftermath_(30_Rock)" title="The Aftermath (30 Rock)">The Aftermath</a>", in which it was also revealed that he has a <a href="/wiki/Thyroid" title="Thyroid">thyroid</a> problem. The J is revealed to stand for Johnny (or John) in "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>". He attended <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin College</a>; after his junior year, he traveled to <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> (a film, interactive, and music festival in Austin, Texas). The show implies that he is a gay man in the process of coming out, although everyone ignores (or forgets) this due to their dislike of him. Lutz periodically mentions a girlfriend who lives in Canada, named Karen. No one believes him; therefore, Lutz created a website (<a class="external text" href="http://jdlutz.com/karen/proof/" rel="nofollow">JDLutz.com/karen/proof</a>‚Äîan actual page on the <i>30 Rock</i> website). He finally identifies himself as bisexual while shouting at his fellow writers on their last day of work in "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>". It is also mentioned during season six that <a href="/wiki/Kellan_Lutz" title="Kellan Lutz">Kellan Lutz</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Twilight_(novel_series)" title="Twilight (novel series)"><i>Twilight</i> series</a> is his grandnephew, and while everyone thinks this is another one of his lies, Kellan actually does show up in Season 7 to hang out with his relative (and to try and tape a pro-Obama skit for TGS). In the series finale, Lutz finally takes revenge on the writing staff after seven years of ridicule by insisting that their final free lunch will be ordered from <a href="/wiki/Blimpie" title="Blimpie">Blimpies</a>, going to absurd lengths to ensure his victory, including legally changing his name to <b>Johnny Aardvark</b> so he will be first alphabetically. Lutz's mother is portrayed by John Lutz in drag in "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>"; however, this may just be the character Lutz impersonating his own mother, since they are not seen together.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Josh_Girard">Josh Girard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Josh Girard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/170px-Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/255px-Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/340px-Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lonny_Ross_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lonny Ross as Josh Girard</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Josh Girard</b> (<a href="/wiki/Lonny_Ross" title="Lonny Ross">Lonny Ross</a>) was the male star of <i>TGS</i> before Tracy was hired. Liz found him while he was opening for a puppet. He, Tracy, and Jenna Maroney are the three main actors on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Show-within-a-show" title="Show-within-a-show">show-within-a-show</a> from Seasons 1 through 3. It has been said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2014)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> that his character is based on <i>SNL</i> alumnus <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fallon" title="Jimmy Fallon">Jimmy Fallon</a>. Josh is frequently seen in the writer's room, and appears to be the only member of the TGS cast who also works as a writer for the show. Often referred to as being a "kid," Josh is described in dialogue in a way that implies he is young, guileless, and unintelligent. He is indeed typically portrayed as lacking smarts and is often shown doing things that are considered juvenile.</p>
<p>Most of Josh's work on the show seems to be as an impressionist; he has performed impressions of <a href="/wiki/Ray_Romano" title="Ray Romano">Ray Romano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stone_Phillips" title="Stone Phillips">Stone Phillips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Taylor" title="Elizabeth Taylor">Elizabeth Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Seinfeld" title="Jerry Seinfeld">Jerry Seinfeld</a>.</p>
<p>His impressions have raised eyebrows from people who are not impressed, like Elizabeth Taylor (played by <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Dratch" title="Rachel Dratch">Rachel Dratch</a>), who knocked him out with an extinguisher and leaving him severely concussed after he did a sketch that offended her in which he impersonated the actress. Original characters that he plays on the show include "Dr. Ridiculous," a Chinese man named Mr. Wang, and Gaybraham Lincoln. In "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>," Tracy got mad at Josh for impersonating him, claiming that Josh was turning him into a caricature. In "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hard_Ball_(30_Rock)" title="Hard Ball (30 Rock)">Hard Ball</a>," it is implied that Josh is Jewish, and in a carry-over during "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>," from the "Secret Rodney" ads that were running, Kenneth says "Merry Jewish" to Josh when passing out gifts. He, Frank, and Toofer are often observed fooling around and admiring Cerie.</p>
<p>In the episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Break-Up_(30_Rock)" title="The Break-Up (30 Rock)">The Break-Up</a>," Josh states that his parents raised him as a girl for 10 years. Jack Donaghy mentions in the show's second episode that Josh had a 760 SAT score and graduated from <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Cortland" title="State University of New York at Cortland">SUNY Cortland</a>. In "Hard Ball," Josh's agent Alan Steiner is introduced. In sharp contrast to Josh, Steiner was portrayed as slick and cunning. Steiner uses unnecessary abbreviations and has a "really bad sex addiction."</p>
<p>In "<a href="/wiki/The_Rural_Juror" title="The Rural Juror">The Rural Juror</a>," Josh snuck into Liz's office to get her copy of <i>The Rural Juror</i> and quickly dislikes it upon seeing the title ("Well, this is disappointing...I had to let Tony [the security guard] watch me pee to get that tape").</p>
<p>In "<a href="/wiki/Season_4_(30_Rock)" title="Season 4 (30 Rock)">Season 4</a>," Josh gets fed up with everyone's poor treatment of him and quits <i>TGS</i>. He then winds up auditioning again in "<a href="/wiki/Audition_Day" title="Audition Day">Audition Day</a>," but he gets rejected; Danny Baker replaces him in the main <i>TGS</i> cast. Lonny Ross was written out of the series in season four. He does appear via a flashback to a raunchy TGS sketch with Tracy in the series finale.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_GE.2FNBC.2FKabletown_employees">Recurring GE/NBC/Kabletown employees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Recurring GE/NBC/Kabletown employees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Danny_Baker">Danny Baker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Danny Baker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1264" data-file-width="968" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg/170px-Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg/255px-Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg/340px-Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne_Jackson_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cheyenne Jackson portrays Danny Baker</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Jack "Danny" Baker</b> (<a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Jackson" title="Cheyenne Jackson">Cheyenne Jackson</a>) is hired as a new <i>TGS</i> cast member in the fourth season. Danny is originally from <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, and after starring in a movie about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Football" title="Canadian Football">Canadian Football</a>, came to New York and became a robotic street performer. He first appears in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Audition_Day" title="Audition Day">Audition Day</a>" (played by actor/dancer Daniel Genalo). On his first day of work (without his silver clothes and makeup), Jack Donaghy renames him 'Danny' rather than have two Jacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Problem_Solvers_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Problem_Solvers-10">[10]</a></sup> Later that day, he accurately speculates to an incredulous Tracy and Jenna that Kenneth could be running the network in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Problem_Solvers_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Problem_Solvers-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Danny had a brief fling with his boss, Liz Lemon, which annoyed Jack. Ironically, it was Jack's example that inspired Liz to "take her reward" with her employee in the first place. Assuming that Danny's real name of Jack is a diminutive of Jon or John (as it is with Donaghy, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">Kennedy</a>, and former GE Chairman <a href="/wiki/Jack_Welch" title="Jack Welch">Jack Welch</a>), he is in keeping with Liz's tendency to date men who share names with celebrities and fictional characters: the <i><a href="/wiki/CHiPs" title="CHiPs">CHiPs</a></i> character portrayed by Liz's childhood crush, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Wilcox" title="Larry Wilcox">Larry Wilcox</a>. Indeed, Danny was even in-costume as Wilcox/Baker during one of their assignations. Jack persuaded Danny to end the affair by telling Danny that he (Jack) was in love with Liz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Danny is earnest, good-natured, and a talented singer. He defers to Jenna when his singing talent makes her jealous, to the point of deliberately singing badly during a Christmas special so she can step in and shine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-9">[9]</a></sup> He mentions that he has a hard time recognizing sarcasm because "Canada has a small Jewish population", and was shocked to discover he was adopted despite his mother being Japanese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Danny doesn't appear in much of the sixth season until he returns in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", in which he reveals that he has been locked in a prison in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> due to the discovery of a suspicious package he was possessing, which happened to have been given to him by Jenna. He makes his final appearance in "<a href="/wiki/There%27s_No_I_in_America" title="There's No I in America">There's No I in America</a>", when he asks Liz to help him from getting deported back to Canada, but Liz ignores his problem.</p>
<p>Appears In: "<a href="/wiki/The_Problem_Solvers" title="The Problem Solvers">The Problem Solvers</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Santa_(30_Rock)" title="Secret Santa (30 Rock)">Secret Santa</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Black_Light_Attack!" title="Black Light Attack!">Black Light Attack!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Winter_Madness" title="Winter Madness">Winter Madness</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Floyd_(30_Rock)" title="Floyd (30 Rock)">Floyd</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mrs._Donaghy" title="Mrs. Donaghy">Mrs. Donaghy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", "<a href="/wiki/There%27s_No_I_in_America" title="There's No I in America">There's No I in America</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Don_Geiss">Don Geiss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Don Geiss">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Don Geiss</b> (<a href="/wiki/Rip_Torn" title="Rip Torn">Rip Torn</a>) <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">…°</span><span title="/a…™/ long 'i' in 'tide'">a…™</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">GYS</span></span></b></i></a></span> is <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> of <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> (GE) on the show, and Jack's boss. Jack considers Geiss his mentor, and idolizes him. Geiss has a mentally challenged daughter (Kathy), an effeminate son (Bertram, 'Daddy's Fancy Boy'), a secret second family in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (a reference to Torn's role in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eulogy_(movie)" title="Eulogy (movie)">Eulogy</a></i>) and a third (secret) attic family. In "<a href="/wiki/Future_Husband" title="Future Husband">Future Husband</a>" Geiss dies, but (real-world) former GE chairman <a href="/wiki/Jack_Welch" title="Jack Welch">Jack Welch</a> keeps his death a secret while GE negotiates a takeover with the (fictional) <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>-based cable company Kabletown (which is based on <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>). Geiss is <a href="/wiki/Cryonics" title="Cryonics">cryogenically</a> frozen in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbonite_(Star_Wars)" title="Carbonite (Star Wars)">carbonite</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal</a> service.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/The_C_Word" title="The C Word">The C Word</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Corporate_Crush" title="Corporate Crush">Corporate Crush</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sandwich_Day" title="Sandwich Day">Sandwich Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Reunion_(30_Rock)" title="Reunion (30 Rock)">Reunion</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Larry_King_(30_Rock)" title="Larry King (30 Rock)">Larry King</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kathy_Geiss">Kathy Geiss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Kathy Geiss">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Kathy Geiss</b> (Marceline Hugot) is Don Geiss' daughter. She is a strange and eccentric middle aged woman and appears to suffer from <a href="/wiki/Rosacea" title="Rosacea">rosacea</a>. Kathy likes <a href="/wiki/Unicorn" title="Unicorn">unicorns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soap_opera" title="Soap opera">soap operas</a>. She is mentally deficient, sometimes harms herself and is oblivious to fiance Devon Banks' blatant homosexuality and contempt for her. She has been seen putting pocket watches and toy race cars in her mouth and eating flowers. She rarely speaks, very occasionally saying single words (such as "kiss kiss kiss" in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do-Over_(30_Rock)" title="Do-Over (30 Rock)">Do-Over</a>"), but is a highly gifted singer and musician, once performing a beautiful rendition of "<a href="/wiki/I_Dreamed_a_Dream" title="I Dreamed a Dream">I Dreamed a Dream</a>", in a send-up of the <a href="/wiki/Susan_Boyle" title="Susan Boyle">Susan Boyle</a> performance, and later performing "Ave Maria" as a trumpet solo. When her father was in a coma, Kathy held the titles of Chairman and CEO of GE and President of East Coast Television and Microwave Oven Programming. In truth, Kathy was only a <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">figurehead</a>, while her fiance (Devon Banks) ran the company from behind the scenes. Her appearance in "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>" suggests that she has taken over GE after her father's death. In "Idiots Are People Three!", it is revealed that she has a "<a href="/wiki/Hug_machine" title="Hug machine">calming box</a>". She later agrees with Jack and Devon to give money to a hospital in exchange that NBC's new mascot be "Majellica the Unicorn". Her invention of a machine to hug the elderly is defective and implied to have crushed an old woman to death.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sandwich_Day" title="Sandwich Day">Sandwich Day</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do-Over_(30_Rock)" title="Do-Over (30 Rock)">Do-Over</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Reunion_(30_Rock)" title="Reunion (30 Rock)">Reunion</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Audition_Day" title="Audition Day">Audition Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Don_Geiss,_America_and_Hope" title="Don Geiss, America and Hope">Don Geiss, America and Hope</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Argus_(30_Rock)" title="Argus (30 Rock)">Argus</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Devon_Banks">Devon Banks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Devon Banks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2348" data-file-width="1878" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG/170px-Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG/255px-Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG/340px-Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Will_Arnett_2012_Shankbone.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Will Arnett as Devon Banks</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Devon Banks</b> (<a href="/wiki/Will_Arnett" title="Will Arnett">Will Arnett</a>) is the former Vice President of West Coast News, Web Content, and Theme Park Talent Relations for <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>. In a 2008 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine, Tina Fey said that Banks' character was based on former co-chairman of NBC Entertainment <a href="/wiki/Ben_Silverman" title="Ben Silverman">Ben Silverman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Devon is the nemesis of the (older) <a href="/wiki/Jack_Donaghy" title="Jack Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</a>; he is first seen in "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>", when his surprise visit from <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> leads Jack to believe that he is trying to take Jack's job as Vice President of East Coast Television and Microwave Oven Programming. Devon is gay, but for a point, was closeted as he becomes engaged to Kathy Geiss in order to get ahead in the company. Devon lusts after <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Parcell" title="Kenneth Parcell">Kenneth Parcell</a> and uses his status as a former <a href="/wiki/NBC_page" title="NBC page">NBC page</a> himself to ingratiate himself with Kenneth. Jack, however, uses Kenneth as a honey trap to spy on and distract Devon. After the events of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do-Over_(30_Rock)" title="Do-Over (30 Rock)">"Do-Over"</a>, he leaves Kathy and winds up showing up again in "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Crevasse" title="Into the Crevasse">Into the Crevasse</a>" working for the Obama administration, and attempts to make Jack take government bail-out money, which Jack eventually does with reluctance. He appears again in Season 5's <a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(30_Rock)" title="Plan B (30 Rock)">"Plan B"</a>, married and the father of three "gaybies" whom he and his partner Cashmere had via a surrogate mother. He briefly attempts to compete with Jack for the CEO position of Kabletown, but learns to treasure family more, and officially admits defeat to Jack. He returns in "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>" and manipulates Jack into using his connections to get his children into an elite preschool, but his joy that Jack won't be able to do that for his own daughter vanishes as Jack smugly notes that Liddy is already brilliant and doesn't need any artificial help. Banks appears again in Season 7's "Game Over" as part of Kaylie Hooper's ploy to wrangle control of Kabletown away from Jack.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do-Over_(30_Rock)" title="Do-Over (30 Rock)">Do-Over</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Crevasse" title="Into the Crevasse">Into the Crevasse</a>, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show #0001</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(30_Rock)" title="Plan B (30 Rock)">Plan B</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hank_Hooper">Hank Hooper</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Hank Hooper">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Hank Hooper</b> (<a href="/wiki/Ken_Howard" title="Ken Howard">Ken Howard</a>), a "family man" and Vietnam veteran, is head of Kabletown. He is often angered by Jack's handling of <i>TGS</i>, but paradoxically always seems happy on the surface (laughing incessantly, while directing thinly-veiled insults and threats to Jack and his staff). He is loosely based on the similarly alliteratively-named founder of <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Roberts" title="Ralph J. Roberts">Ralph J. Roberts</a>; Comcast is sometimes said to be run as a "family business.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vision_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-vision-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/%C2%A1Qu%C3%A9_Sorpresa!" title="¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!">¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(30_Rock)" title="Plan B (30 Rock)">Plan B</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Ballad_of_Kenneth_Parcell" title="The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell">The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Standards_and_Practices_(30_Rock)" title="Standards and Practices (30 Rock)">Standards and Practices</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Shower_Principle" title="The Shower Principle">The Shower Principle</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subhas">Subhas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Subhas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Subhas</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Subhas_Ramsaywack&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Subhas Ramsaywack (page does not exist)">Subhas Ramsaywack</a>) is the head janitor at 30 Rockefeller Plaza. He is an Indian immigrant and is married to <a href="/wiki/Ann_Curry" title="Ann Curry">Ann Curry</a>. Subhas is central to a plot arc in Season 4 parodying the feud between late-night television hosts <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conan_O%27Brien" title="Conan O'Brien">Conan O'Brien</a>. In 2005, Jack Donaghy had signed a contract with Subhas' rival Indian janitor, Khonani, to take over the 11:30¬†p.m. janitorial shift from Subhas in five years' time. In "<a href="/wiki/Khonani" title="Khonani">Khonani</a>", it's 2010 and Jack informs Subhas the deal is taking effect. After Subhas objects, Jack agrees to move him to 10:00¬†p.m. Khonani however then protests to Jack that there is no trash for him to pick up at 11:30 because Subhas has already collected it. Ultimately, Subhas returns to 11:30 and Khonani leaves NBC for "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FOX_Broadcasting_Company" title="FOX Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> [cough] -woods ... Foxwoods Resort Casino."</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Crevasse" title="Into the Crevasse">Into the Crevasse</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Santa_(30_Rock)" title="Secret Santa (30 Rock)">Secret Santa</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Khonani" title="Khonani">Khonani</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Gentleman%27s_Intermission" title="Gentleman's Intermission">Gentleman's Intermission</a>", "<a href="/wiki/%C2%A1Qu%C3%A9_Sorpresa!" title="¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!">¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/TGS_Hates_Women" title="TGS Hates Women">TGS Hates Women</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Heart_Connecticut" title="I Heart Connecticut">I Heart Connecticut</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Two!" title="Idiots Are People Two!">Idiots Are People Two!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kaylie_Hooper">Kaylie Hooper</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Kaylie Hooper">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5,_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2789" data-file-width="2102" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg/170px-Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg/255px-Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg/340px-Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chlo%C3%AB_Moretz_5,_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chlo√´ Grace Moretz portrays Kaylie Hooper</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Kaylie Hooper</b> (<a href="/wiki/Chlo%C3%AB_Grace_Moretz" title="Chlo√´ Grace Moretz">Chlo√´ Grace Moretz</a>) is the granddaughter of Hank Hooper, who is in competition with Jack to take over her grandfather's role as CEO of Kabletown. First introduced in "<a href="/wiki/TGS_Hates_Women" title="TGS Hates Women">TGS Hates Women</a>", she has twice used typical teenage girl antics to try to cover up her schemes to bring down Jack. Initially, she pretended to be interested in oceanography and later threatened to destroy Jack if he interfered with her future at Kabletown. Later on, she deliberately sabotaged an NBC reality show with singing kids as part of a convoluted plot to make sure Jack got her expelled from a private school she hated, thus landing her a spot at a school in Manhattan with her NYU student boyfriend‚Äîbut Jack got the last laugh, as he ruined her dreams of playing lacrosse there and she couldn't pretend he hadn't won that round. Kaylie returns in "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>", still wanting to be CEO of Kabletown. In this episode, it is apparently revealed that she is not Hank's granddaughter and Jack plans to expose her. In reality, she is Hank's granddaughter and that she deliberately set up Jack to try to make him send her DNA to Hank when he actually sent him someone else's DNA, using Devon as a pawn in her plan. However, Jack revealed that he never sent Hank her DNA but instead a birthday card for Hank, something that Hank is very passionate about and something that Kaylie did not do due to being distracted by Jack throughout the whole week, sealing Jack's fate as Kabletown CEO and Kaylie's ultimate downfall.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/TGS_Hates_Women" title="TGS Hates Women">TGS Hates Women</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Standards_and_Practices_(30_Rock)" title="Standards and Practices (30 Rock)">Standards and Practices</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Howard_Jorgensen">Howard Jorgensen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Howard Jorgensen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Howard Jorgensen</b> (<a href="/wiki/Brian_Stack" title="Brian Stack">Brian Stack</a>) is Vice President of Locomotives at GE and a member of the board of directors. A former prot√©g√© of Jack's, he is married to a Filipina woman, has two children and owns a house with a pool. Jack has stated that people use Jorgensen as a scapegoat.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Meets_Dennis" title="Jack Meets Dennis">Jack Meets Dennis</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Larry_King_(30_Rock)" title="Larry King (30 Rock)">Larry King</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Donny_Lawson">Donny Lawson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Donny Lawson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Donny Lawson</b> (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Scheer" title="Paul Scheer">Paul Scheer</a>) is the head page at 30 Rockefeller Plaza, known for his weak one-liners and bizarre hand gestures. He despises Kenneth for his cheerfulness, and wants to transfer him to the <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> studios in <a href="/wiki/Paramus,_New_Jersey" title="Paramus, New Jersey">Paramus</a>. Donny was introduced on the series when Jenna tries to find a replacement jacket for Kenneth; Donny uses this as an excuse to give Kenneth a demerit. He challenges him to a "page-off" (a strange contest, mixing physical stamina with NBC trivia) which is quickly broken up by Pete, who orders Donny to give Kenneth a new jacket.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Rosemary%27s_Baby_(30_Rock)" title="Rosemary's Baby (30 Rock)">Rosemary's Baby</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cooter_(30_Rock)" title="Cooter (30 Rock)">Cooter</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jeffrey_Weinerslav">Jeffrey Weinerslav</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Jeffrey Weinerslav">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Jeffrey Weinerslav</b> (Todd Buonopane) (pronounced "weener-slave") works for GE <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a>. He tried to mediate a dispute between Jenna and Tracy, but failed. Weinerslav is a self-described "overweight <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a>". He counseled Liz during her forced leave for <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a> (which she attempted to extend by making a pass at him). He later counsels Jack and Liz when they briefly get married due to a clerical error.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Believe_in_the_Stars" title="Believe in the Stars">Believe in the Stars</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cutbacks_(30_Rock)" title="Cutbacks (30 Rock)">Cutbacks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jackie_Jormp-Jomp" title="Jackie Jormp-Jomp">Jackie Jormp-Jomp</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Stay_Together_(30_Rock)" title="Let's Stay Together (30 Rock)">Let's Stay Together</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mrs._Donaghy" title="Mrs. Donaghy">Mrs. Donaghy</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hazel_Wassername">Hazel Wassername</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hazel Wassername">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2929" data-file-width="2118" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg/170px-Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg/255px-Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg/340px-Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kristen_Schaal_3_BBF_2010_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kristen Schaal portrays Hazel Wassername</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Hazel Wassername,</b> aka Richard Drench (<a href="/wiki/Kristen_Schaal" title="Kristen Schaal">Kristen Schaal</a>) replaces Kenneth as an NBC page when he is promoted to Standards and Practice.
