At first, she stalked Liz and deeply despised Jenna, having nearly succeeded in her efforts to maim or kill her and therefore become Liz's "best friend". In "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>" it is revealed that she sees Kenneth as a threat, and rewrites his reapplication to the page program in a way that causes him to not receive the job. She also moves in with him in the same episode, and while her claim that she's "in love" with him appears to be false, she is the only woman he has ever been seen kissing on the show. She previously had a relationship with a pimp named Razmig, and has some disturbing sexual notions. She is a recurring character, beginning in season six. In "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", she reveals that she left her kids in a <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> in 2004 and has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IQ" title="IQ">IQ</a> of 70, though considering her penchant for lying and exaggeration, it is possible that these claims are both false. She was later fired by Liz for attempting to trick Pete into letting her perform on TGS. Before leaving, she reveals that Hazel Wassername is not her real name. Following her departure, Hazel breaks up with Kenneth. In "<a href="/wiki/My_Whole_Life_Is_Thunder" title="My Whole Life Is Thunder">My Whole Life Is Thunder</a>", Hazel is "recast" by Tracy as a young Asian woman (Shannon Tyo) in an attempt to cheer Kenneth up.</p>
<p>After leaving NBC, Wassername sues parent company Kabletown alleging to have been the victim of sexual harassment in "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>". Although her claims make her look worse than any of her co-workers, she accurately recounts how badly everyone treats Kenneth; when Jenna and Tracy tell him to be honest, he confirms those incidents (though he isn't that upset about them) and the bad publicity leads Hank Hooper to finally cancel TGS.</p>
<p><i>Appears in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Today_You_Are_a_Man" title="Today You Are a Man">Today You Are a Man</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>", "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Grandmentor" title="Grandmentor">Grandmentor</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Shower_Principle" title="The Shower Principle">The Shower Principle</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Beginning_of_the_End_(30_Rock)" title="The Beginning of the End (30 Rock)">The Beginning of the End</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Aunt_Phatso_vs._Jack_Donaghy" title="Aunt Phatso vs. Jack Donaghy">Aunt Phatso vs. Jack Donaghy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greta_Johansen">Greta Johansen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Greta Johansen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Legreta "Greta" Johansen</b> (<a href="/wiki/Rachel_Dratch" title="Rachel Dratch">Rachel Dratch</a>) is a cat <a href="/wiki/Wrangler_(profession)" title="Wrangler (profession)">wrangler</a> who works on the show. In "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>" she offered to carry the child whom Liz wants, and revealed that she owns a small ferret farm 60 miles (97¬†km) north of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. Greta hints at an obsession with Liz, mentioning that she likes to watch Liz watching TV. <i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Pilot_(30_Rock)" title="Pilot (30 Rock)">Pilot</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_C_Word" title="The C Word">The C Word</a>," "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>"</p>
<p>Dratch, who was featured as Jenna in the original pilot of the show but recast, has also played several minor characters, predominantly in season 1, including <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a> ("<a href="/wiki/The_Rural_Juror" title="The Rural Juror">The Rural Juror</a>"), <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Taylor" title="Elizabeth Taylor">Elizabeth Taylor</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Jack_Meets_Dennis" title="Jack Meets Dennis">Jack Meets Dennis</a>"), a Latina maid ("<a href="/wiki/The_Aftermath_(30_Rock)" title="The Aftermath (30 Rock)">The Aftermath</a>"), a drunken Russian prostitute ("<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>"), Liz's doctor ("<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>"), a protestor ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hard_Ball_(30_Rock)" title="Hard Ball (30 Rock)">Hard Ball</a>"), a group therapist ("<a href="/wiki/The_Break-Up_(30_Rock)" title="The Break-Up (30 Rock)">The Break-Up</a>"), the <a href="/wiki/Happy_Days" title="Happy Days">Happy Days</a>-obsessed janitor, Jadwiga, in the season-five episode "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>", the voice of an NBC-trivia spouting computer called Not Kenneth (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Ballad_of_Kenneth_Parcell" title="The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell">The Ballad of Kenneth Parcell</a></i>), and a "little blue dude" seen in hallucinations in "<a href="/wiki/Tracy_Does_Conan" title="Tracy Does Conan">Tracy Does Conan</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sue_LaRoche-Van_der_Hout">Sue LaRoche-Van der Hout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sue LaRoche-Van der Hout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Susannah "Sue" LaRoche-Van der Hout</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sue_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sue Galloway (page does not exist)">Sue Galloway</a>), also referred to as "girl-writer", is a <i>TGS</i> writer, who speaks with a heavy <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> accent. The <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> dramatic series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mentalist" title="The Mentalist">The Mentalist</a></i>, is a remake of a Dutch programme, <i>Van der Hoot: Psychische (De Mentalist)</i>, which was based upon Sue's work as a police psychic in The Netherlands. Following the cancellation of <i>TGS With Tracy Jordan</i>, she takes a serving position at <a href="/wiki/Hooters" title="Hooters">Hooters</a> despite being heavily pregnant; she is called back for the final <i>TGS</i> episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hogcock.21_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hogcock.21-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Last_Lunch_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Last_Lunch-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sue has a pragmatic personality, but she is known for unpredictable behavior. She appears to have an affinity for <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">pornography</a>, and some episodes allude that she is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a>. She apparently has a <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Black</a> daughter, whom she brings to work on Take Your Black Kid to Work Day in "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>". Sue also claims that she is a virgin ("with white guys") when offering herself to Jack in "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>". In "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Light_Attack_(30_Rock)" title="Black Light Attack (30 Rock)">Black Light Attack</a>", Tracy adds her to his entourage, seeking a woman's influence after he learns he is going to have a daughter; she soon, however, leaves the entourage in anger after Tracy begins to act like an overprotective father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Black_Light_Attack.21_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Light_Attack.21-17">[17]</a></sup> In "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Never_Too_Late_for_Now" title="It's Never Too Late for Now">It's Never Too Late for Now</a>", it is shown that she can become very violent: when Jack hires the writers to stage a fake fight, she beats up Lutz and even breaks Toofer's arm and her own wrist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-It.27s_Never_Too_Late_for_Now_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-It.27s_Never_Too_Late_for_Now-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Notable appearances</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Special_(30_Rock)" title="Christmas Special (30 Rock)">Christmas Special</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Funcooker" title="The Funcooker">The Funcooker</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Crevasse" title="Into the Crevasse">Into the Crevasse</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Mountain_(30_Rock)" title="Stone Mountain (30 Rock)">Stone Mountain</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show#0001" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show#0001</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Black_Light_Attack!" title="Black Light Attack!">Black Light Attack!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Winter_Madness" title="Winter Madness">Winter Madness</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Stride_of_Pride" title="Stride of Pride">Stride of Pride</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaylord_Felcher">Gaylord Felcher</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Gaylord Felcher">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Gaylord Felcher</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Torpey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michael Torpey (page does not exist)">Michael Torpey</a>) is the head of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standards_and_Practices" title="Standards and Practices">Standards and Practices</a> at NBC. Felcher is Kenneth Parcell's boss while he works in Standards and enjoys using profanity and obscene gestures.</p>
<p><i>Appears in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Standards_and_Practices_(30_Rock)" title="Standards and Practices (30 Rock)">Standards and Practices</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Grandmentor" title="Grandmentor">Grandmentor</a>"</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Liz.27s_love_interests">Liz's love interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Liz's love interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following characters have (at some point during the show) been boyfriends of Liz.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dennis_Duffy">Dennis Duffy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Dennis Duffy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DeanWintersOct10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1436" data-file-width="847" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeanWintersOct10.jpg/170px-DeanWintersOct10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeanWintersOct10.jpg/255px-DeanWintersOct10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeanWintersOct10.jpg/340px-DeanWintersOct10.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DeanWintersOct10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dean Winters portrays Dennis Duffy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Dennis Duffy</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dean_Winters" title="Dean Winters">Dean Winters</a>) was Liz's <a href="/wiki/Boyfriend" title="Boyfriend">boyfriend</a> for three episodes during the early part of the show's first season; he has also made appearances in each subsequent season. Liz had a relationship with him that ended prior to the series, and she briefly resumes a relationship with him only to break it off after discovering that he has been featured on <i><a href="/wiki/To_Catch_a_Predator" title="To Catch a Predator">To Catch a Predator</a></i>. (Dennis later claimed that he knew the girl was actually eighteen because, "She said her last boyfriend was Asian, and that crap doesn't start 'till college.") Dennis has popped up occasionally in later seasons to annoy Liz and attempt to get back together. He is generally disliked by most of the characters, most notably by Liz, Jack and Jenna, with whom he once had sex behind Liz's back.</p>
<p>Dennis claims to be the love of Liz's life, which she disputes. The few good memories she has of him are mostly food-related, but she admits he makes her laugh. His nickname for her is "Dummy." She nearly got engaged to him and signed a lease on an apartment in Jacksonville before Jack Donaghy got over a pointless feud with Liz and stopped that. In his last two appearances on the show, Dennis has married an obnoxious Irish-American woman named Megan (whose maiden name is also Duffy) and they have adopted an African-American baby boy whom they call "Black Dennis". While Dennis is worthless, he did inspire Liz to finally declare her love for her new boyfriend Criss Chros and, later, to marry him.</p>
<p>Dennis is immature for a man his age, often exclaiming like a teenage boy. In one episode he sits on Liz's bed, playing <i><a href="/wiki/Halo_3" title="Halo 3">Halo 3</a></i>; then, he throws the controller down and yells that the controller is "defective" because "that grenade was right next to him!" He was the last remaining <a href="/wiki/Pager" title="Pager">beeper</a> salesman in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, and was known as the "Beeper King" (after the original Beeper King committed suicide). His other plans are similarly moronic, including a make-your-own coffee station, copying DVD movies onto <a href="/wiki/LaserDisc" title="LaserDisc">LaserDisc</a>, and the participation in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balloon_Boy" title="Balloon Boy">Balloon Boy</a>-like stunt after being assigned to a program that pairs talented kids with troubled adults. In his final appearance, he brags that he has found success selling "suicide insurance". In the episode "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", it is revealed that his ancestors were kicked out of Ireland, then kicked out of America, sent back to Ireland, then set adrift on a log.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Meets_Dennis" title="Jack Meets Dennis">Jack Meets Dennis</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tracy_Does_Conan" title="Tracy Does Conan">Tracy Does Conan</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Break-Up_(30_Rock)" title="The Break-Up (30 Rock)">The Break-Up</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Subway_Hero" title="Subway Hero">Subway Hero</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cooter_(30_Rock)" title="Cooter (30 Rock)">Cooter</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Apollo,_Apollo" title="Apollo, Apollo">Apollo, Apollo</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Anna_Howard_Shaw_Day" title="Anna Howard Shaw Day">Anna Howard Shaw Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Righteous_Cowboy_Lightning" title="Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning">Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>", "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mazel_Tov,_Dummies!" title="Mazel Tov, Dummies!">Mazel Tov, Dummies!</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Floyd_DeBarber">Floyd DeBarber</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Floyd DeBarber">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1412" data-file-width="1254" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg/170px-Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg/255px-Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg/340px-Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jason_Sudeikis_at_2009_NYTVF.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jason Sudeikis portrays Floyd DeBarber</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Floyd DeBarber</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jason_Sudeikis" title="Jason Sudeikis">Jason Sudeikis</a>) is an attorney working at 30 Rock. His name is a play on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Floyd_the_Barber" title="Floyd the Barber">Floyd the Barber</a>, a regular character on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Andy_Griffith_Show" title="The Andy Griffith Show">The Andy Griffith Show</a></i>. Floyd's first appearance is when he accidentally sends flowers to Liz for <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a>, which he actually intended to send to his girlfriend, Liz Lemler. Liz, who doesn't know his name, calls him "flower guy" and develops a crush on him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floydremote_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Floydremote-19">[19]</a></sup> In "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Fighting_Irish_(30_Rock)" title="The Fighting Irish (30 Rock)">The Fighting Irish</a>," Liz fires Liz Lemler and the rest of the accounting staff so that she can get closer to Floyd, with his girlfriend out of the building; however, Jack rehires the accountants and transfers Liz Lemler to a job at GE headquarters in Connecticut, thus breaking up Liz Lemler and Floyd. In "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>," Liz follows Floyd to an <a href="/wiki/Alcoholics_Anonymous" title="Alcoholics Anonymous">AA</a> meeting in order to get close to him and discovers that rules are important to him. When Liz lies about being an alcoholic so Floyd will confide in her, she discovers that members of the same AA group cannot date; therefore, she confesses she was never an alcoholic and merely had a crush on him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floydpopcandy_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-floydpopcandy-20">[20]</a></sup> Floyd feels betrayed, but Liz makes it up to him by confiding in him and the two then begin dating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floydpopcandy_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-floydpopcandy-20">[20]</a></sup> Jack becomes good friends with Floyd, calling him "the Floydster," much to Liz's dismay. Floyd eventually seems to want to spend more time with Jack than Liz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FilmFloyd_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FilmFloyd-21">[21]</a></sup> At the end of season one, Floyd decides that New York City is too much for him and decides to return to his hometown, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>. Liz and Floyd go there on vacation; Floyd gets a job in Cleveland, and Liz returns to <i>TGS</i> in New York. Despite seeming perfect for each other, Floyd and Liz break up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floydpopcandy_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-floydpopcandy-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FilmFloyd_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FilmFloyd-21">[21]</a></sup> In Season 4, Floyd returns in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Floyd_(30_Rock)" title="Floyd (30 Rock)">Floyd</a>", announcing he is engaged to be married. His wedding eventually takes place in the fourth season finale "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>".</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Source_Awards" title="The Source Awards">The Source Awards</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Fighting_Irish_(30_Rock)" title="The Fighting Irish (30 Rock)">The Fighting Irish</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Corporate_Crush" title="Corporate Crush">Corporate Crush</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cleveland_(30_Rock)" title="Cleveland (30 Rock)">Cleveland</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sandwich_Day" title="Sandwich Day">Sandwich Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Anna_Howard_Shaw_Day" title="Anna Howard Shaw Day">Anna Howard Shaw Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Floyd_(30_Rock)" title="Floyd (30 Rock)">Floyd</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drew_Baird">Drew Baird</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Drew Baird">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="936" data-file-width="876" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg/170px-Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg/255px-Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg/340px-Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jon_Hamm_Vancouver_Olympics_2010_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jon Hamm portrays Drew Baird</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Dr. Andrew "Drew" Baird</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jon_Hamm" title="Jon Hamm">Jon Hamm</a>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pediatrician" title="Pediatrician">pediatrician</a> and Liz's very handsome neighbor. He graduated from <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University_College_of_Physicians_and_Surgeons" title="Columbia University College of Physicians and Surgeons">Columbia University medical school</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">Disney</a> used a photo of him from his high school swim team as a model for Prince Eric in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>. His name is a play on <a href="/wiki/Drew_Pinsky" title="Drew Pinsky">Dr. Drew</a>. He first appears in season three episode "<a href="/wiki/Generalissimo_(30_Rock)" title="Generalissimo (30 Rock)">Generalissimo</a>", when Liz accidentally receives his mail. After going through the contents (which includes a warranty for his ice cream maker and his <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> rentals: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Muppets_Take_Manhattan" title="The Muppets Take Manhattan">The Muppets Take Manhattan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Caddyshack" title="Caddyshack">Caddyshack</a></i>, and a documentary on how pies are made), Liz decides he is perfect for her and creates a false persona so he will like her. Liz's scheme unravels, and Drew is disappointed in her; however, he reads her mail and tells her he feels Liz would have been someone he would have wanted to know. Eventually, they agree upon a fresh start.</p>
<p>He is recently divorced from Mandy and has one daughter from the marriage (Bethany, a rebellious teenager who drinks wine and starts fires). Liz and Drew's first date was on <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a> 2009, during which Bethany ended up at Liz's apartment and Drew's mother died in the hospital. On her deathbed she reveals to Liz that she is not actually Drew's mother; the person Drew thinks is his sister is, in fact, his mother. She asks Liz to tell him the truth and Liz reveals this to Drew later in the episode.</p>
<p>In episode 15 of season three, ("<a href="/wiki/The_Bubble_(30_Rock)" title="The Bubble (30 Rock)">The Bubble</a>"), Liz is concerned about the way others treat Drew; he is so handsome that he unintentionally causes others to fawn over him. He was a professional tennis player in college even though he is terrible at it. Despite being horrible at everything from cooking to sex to not knowing how to perform the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heimlich_maneuver" title="Heimlich maneuver">Heimlich maneuver</a>, no one tells him the truth because he is so good-looking. <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Klein" title="Calvin Klein">Calvin Klein</a> (in a cameo) stops him on the street and asks him to be an underwear model. He never has to wait in line at restaurants; when Liz (blocking Drew's face from view) orders his request off the menu and is berated by the waitress, he is mystified by her response and wonders where their complementary appetizer sampler is. Jack, having firsthand knowledge of the situation from his younger days, describes this as "The Bubble." Liz tells Drew that he receives constant special treatment, and when Liz stops letting him win at tennis, he realizes that he is actually very dimwitted and clumsy, lashing out at her. Eventually he apologizes for his behavior but prefers living in "The Bubble" to reality, asking Liz if she wants to take a ride with him on his new motorcycle. Liz declines and Drew rides into the sunset, careening incompetently down the street.</p>
<p>When Liz goes back to her ex-boyfriends in "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", Drew appears with hooks on both hands: one hand had been lost in a New Year's firework explosion and the other in a helicopter accident, both caused by his stupidity. Drew later reappears in a cameo in season five episode <a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>, having received one replacement hand from a <a href="/wiki/Death_row" title="Death row">death row</a> inmate. The hand has a mind of its own, however, and begins to strangle him (In the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> version of "Live Show", Drew received a female hand transplant that constantly tries to seduce him). Liz later sums up Drew in the phrase "So handsome...so, so stupid."</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Generalissimo_(30_Rock)" title="Generalissimo (30 Rock)">Generalissimo</a>", "<a href="/wiki/St._Valentine%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Valentine's Day (30 Rock)">St Valentine's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Bubble_(30_Rock)" title="The Bubble (30 Rock)">The Bubble</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Anna_Howard_Shaw_Day" title="Anna Howard Shaw Day">Anna Howard Shaw Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>". Jon Hamm also appeared in "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>" playing two roles, but not as Drew.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wesley_Snipes">Wesley Snipes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Wesley Snipes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1280" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg/170px-Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg/255px-Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg/340px-Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Josh_Jensen_-_Michael_Sheen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Michael Sheen portrays Wesley Snipes, an Englishman</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Wesley Snipes</b> (<a href="/wiki/Michael_Sheen" title="Michael Sheen">Michael Sheen</a>) is an Englishman whom Liz meets at her dentist's office while recovering from a root canal operation. Being under the effects of <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a>, they seem to hit it off and list each other in their phones as "Future Husband" and "Future Wife". When sober, they immediately realize that they have nothing in common and dislike each other intensely. However, when they keep meeting each other by chance around the city, they continue to date believing that it is their destiny to "settle" for one another.</p>
<p>Wesley is displeased that the actor <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Snipes" title="Wesley Snipes">Wesley Snipes</a> has his name, saying that the name is better suited to a "pasty, un-athletic British man". He frequently uses (fictional) <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> phrases, such as "foot cycle" for <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">bicycle</a> and "film pod" for <a href="/wiki/Video_camera" title="Video camera">video camera</a>, which annoys Liz. He is rude to her, mocking her disastrous romantic history and at one point compares her life to a "<a href="/wiki/Cathy" title="Cathy">Cathy</a> cartoon that just won't end".</p>
<p>He believes they are "settling soul mates" and sets the stage for another meeting during "Sweeps", which Liz assumes refers to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings#Sweeps" title="Nielsen ratings">television sweeps week</a>, but which he claims is what the British call <a href="/wiki/Spring_cleaning" title="Spring cleaning">spring cleaning</a>. After a tour of her abysmal past relationships, she decides Wesley is her only alternative and reluctantly agrees to get engaged to him. However, in the Season 4 finale Liz meets a pilot, Carol (<a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a>), whom she likes a lot and sends Wesley a break-up text. He stupidly thinks they're getting past their first fight, but Liz tells him she's realized after meeting Carol that she can do much better than Wesley, and says goodbye to him. He leaves the room in defeat and has not been seen since. In a Season 6 episode, a flashback scene has Liz outright telling her tax accountant "I'm having a go at cycling thanks to my boyfriend Wesley, whom I hate."</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Future_Husband" title="Future Husband">Future Husband</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Don_Geiss,_America_and_Hope" title="Don Geiss, America and Hope">Don Geiss, America and Hope</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronaut_Mike_Dexter">Astronaut Mike Dexter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Astronaut Mike Dexter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Astronaut Mike Dexter</b> (John Anderson) is Liz's fantasy boyfriend, to whom she compares all other men; Mike often appears when Liz is either alone or involved in disastrous relationships, and is no longer seen once she develops a (relatively) normal social life. Liz mentions Dexter in several episodes, and he appears in her imagination throughout <a href="/wiki/30_Rock_(season_4)" title="30 Rock (season 4)">Season 4</a>. In a fantasy sequence in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show#0001" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show#0001</a>," Dexter tells Liz he has to go back to space, but "enjoyed the kissing followed by [his] genuine interest in that TV dance competition". In "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", Liz reveals that Astronaut Mike Dexter is also (secretly) king of Monaco. Liz meets an attorney named Mike (also played by Anderson) at <a href="/wiki/List_of_30_Rock_characters#Floyd_DeBarber" title="List of 30 Rock characters">Floyd</a>'s wedding in "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>"; this Mike describes himself as a "<a href="/wiki/Plushophilia" title="Plushophilia">plushie</a>" who enjoys having sex ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiff" title="Yiff">yiffing</a>") with people in mascot costumes at state parks. Anderson also appears, as a nod to Liz's fantasies of Dexter, in an episode of Jack's "Porn for Women" (which features handsome men asking women about their day), which Liz buys. ("<a href="/wiki/Don_Geiss,_America_and_Hope" title="Don Geiss, America and Hope">Don Geiss, America and Hope</a>")</p>
<p>Liz ends her idolization of the fictional astronaut after learning of her mother's premarital relationship with <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">Buzz Aldrin</a> (recreated in Liz's fantasy flashback by Fey and Anderson) and discussing the matter with present-day Aldrin in "The Moms".</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show#0001" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show#0001</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Don_Geiss,_America_and_Hope" title="Don Geiss, America and Hope">Don Geiss, America and Hope</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carol_Burnett">Carol Burnett</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Carol Burnett">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Carol Burnett</b> (<a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a>) is an airline pilot who begins a relationship with Liz in the <a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">season four finale</a>. With an identical name to the <a href="/wiki/Carol_Burnett" title="Carol Burnett">television comedian's</a>, he is her second consecutive boyfriend with the same name as a celebrity (after Wesley Snipes). Their first date takes place after he learns that Liz is the head writer of <i>TGS with Tracy Jordan,</i> and she finds out that Carol is an enthusiastic fan of the show, often showing episodes on his flights. Liz enjoys their relationship at first because his frequent absences for work gives her freedom. Carol, however, is eager to settle down and pursue a more normal relationship, since every relationship he has had as an airline pilot were intermittent affairs due to his constant travel for work.</p>
<p>Initially, Liz believes their similar personalities make them soul mates after they repeatedly share the same responses to games of "<a href="/wiki/Would_you_rather" title="Would you rather">Would you rather</a>". However they eventually realize that they are too similar, and in "<a href="/wiki/Double-Edged_Sword_(30_Rock)" title="Double-Edged Sword (30 Rock)">Double-Edged Sword</a>", their equally controlling personalities come to a head after a heated argument while being stuck for hours on the runway on a plane piloted by Carol.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Fabian_Strategy" title="The Fabian Strategy">The Fabian Strategy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Double-Edged_Sword_(30_Rock)" title="Double-Edged Sword (30 Rock)">Double-Edged Sword</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criss_Chros">Criss Chros</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Criss Chros">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank,_January_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="463" data-file-width="338" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank%2C_January_2012.jpg/170px-James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank%2C_January_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank%2C_January_2012.jpg/255px-James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank%2C_January_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/55/James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank%2C_January_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:James_Marsden_at_the_World_Premiere_of_Robot_and_Frank,_January_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James Marsden portrays Criss Chros</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Crisstopher Rick Chros</b> (<a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a>) is an unemployed entrepreneur, and like <a href="#Dot_Com">Dot Com</a>, attended <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_University" title="Wesleyan University">Wesleyan University</a>. He dropped out of law school, but holds a degree in ethnomusicology. He and Liz met somewhere between the end of season five and the beginning of season 6 at Riverside Park after Liz made fun of his turtleneck shirt. He runs a hot dog stand which sells organic hot dogs. It is revealed that he and Liz are dating in "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Two!" title="Idiots Are People Two!">Idiots Are People Two!</a>" and that Liz has kept it a secret from Jack because she fears he'll disapprove of Criss - which Jack does, at first, but winds up changing his mind and gives Criss his "probational approval" card in "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>" In "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", a surprise visit from <a href="#Dennis_Duffy">Dennis</a> makes Liz finally admit that she is in love with Criss after an argument. When she tells him that she loves him, something she has never done to anyone, Criss responds by quoting <a href="/wiki/Han_Solo" title="Han Solo">Han Solo</a>'s response to <a href="/wiki/Princess_Leia" title="Princess Leia">Princess Leia</a>, "I know," thereby proving his suitability to the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i>-obsessed Liz.</p>
<p>Jack sets up Liz on a "blind date" with Kevin, a man Jack actually hates, but his true purpose is to introduce Liz to Kevin's "awesome" Lemon-esque young daughter (Bebe Wood). After realizing that having children might be a good thing, Criss and Liz subsequently "put a pin" in this idea and decide to "just have some fun". Still, Criss is insecure in their relationship, believing that Liz might eventually bail on him. In the episode "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>", Criss sells his hot dog van to help pay for renovating Liz's apartment. Unfortunately he sells the van to "a really nice young guy on meth", who later steals money from a bank. Liz sees what she thinks is still Criss's van on a TV news report on the robbery, and thinking that Criss stole the money, tells him she will go to prison in his place. Criss considers this a sign that Liz will not bail on him, and later in the episode, when Liz observes that the room Criss is renovating will make a great nursery, they both realize that they are ready to try for a baby, whether biological or adopted.</p>
<p>As of Season 7, he and Liz are actively trying to have a child. Liz's unusual libido starts to make things a bit difficult, but they eventually find what works for them both. After a failed pregnancy test, Liz and Criss decide to get married in order to make an adoption process easier. They are married in a brief ceremony at City Hall attended by Jack, Dennis Duffy and his family, two homeless men and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a>.</p>
<p>Liz and Criss eventually adopt a pair of elementary-school aged twins, Janet and Terry (who are highly reminiscent of Tracy and Jenna). Criss briefly goes to work as a dental receptionist, but discovers he much prefers being a stay-at-home father.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Two!" title="Idiots Are People Two!">Idiots Are People Two!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Idiots_Are_People_Three!" title="Idiots Are People Three!">Idiots Are People Three!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Leap_Day_(30_Rock)" title="Leap Day (30 Rock)">Leap Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Patrick's Day (30 Rock)">St. Patrick's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Murphy_Brown_Lied_to_Us" title="Murphy Brown Lied to Us">Murphy Brown Lied to Us</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_Avery_Jessup" title="The Return of Avery Jessup">The Return of Avery Jessup</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Governor_Dunston" title="Governor Dunston">Governor Dunston</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mazel_Tov,_Dummies!" title="Mazel Tov, Dummies!">Mazel Tov, Dummies!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liz.27s_one-episode_love_interests">Liz's one-episode love interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Liz's one-episode love interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Gretchen Thomas</b> (<a href="/wiki/Stephanie_March" title="Stephanie March">Stephanie March</a>) is a "brilliant plastics engineer / lesbian" and a friend of Jack Donaghy from his rotation in General Electric's plastics division. Assuming Liz to be bisexual if not a lesbian (and maintaining that her shoes are "definitely bi-curious"), Jack sets up the pair on a blind date in "<a href="/wiki/Blind_Date_(30_Rock)" title="Blind Date (30 Rock)">Blind Date</a>". When proposing the idea to Liz, Jack refers to her simply as 'Thomas' (much as he generally addresses Liz by her surname, Lemon), and Liz is thus unaware of Gretchen's gender until meeting her. Despite Liz's lack of sexual attraction toward Gretchen, the two bond over dinner and Gretchen informs Jack that she finds Liz "great" and thinks she looks like <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Jason_Leigh" title="Jennifer Jason Leigh">Jennifer Jason Leigh</a>. They enjoy a succession of platonic dates until Gretchen expresses that she feels she is starting to chase the straight girl and decides they should stop seeing each other. Liz attempts to make a pact that they get back together after 25 years and start a relationship then if they are both still single (including an offer to let Gretchen "do stuff to [her]" as long as Liz is not expected to reciprocate), but Gretchen walks away.</li>
<li><b>Gray</b> (<a href="/wiki/Peter_Hermann_(actor)" title="Peter Hermann (actor)">Peter Hermann</a>) appears in a season one episode as a tall, handsome and well-coiffed stranger Jenna and Liz keep bumping into at the 30 Rock building and refer to as "The Hair." When Liz and Gray finally meet, they trade witty banter and discover they share similar likes and annoyances. Although they seem to click, Liz cannot escape the feeling that their disparate levels of attractiveness make her unworthy to be with him. During a date that begins to turn romantic at Gray's apartment, Liz spots a photo of a mutual relative and they realize to their dismay that they're actually distant cousins. Liz shuts it down but before she leaves, Gray assures her that she is also a "hair."</li>
<li><b>Steven Black</b> (<a href="/wiki/Wayne_Brady" title="Wayne Brady">Wayne Brady</a>) was Tracy's manager during season one. He briefly dated Liz during "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Source_Awards" title="The Source Awards">The Source Awards</a>", but Liz realized that they were incompatible after one date. When she attempted to break things off, Steven claimed that she was racist. Liz continued to date Steven, hoping he would see their incompatibility for himself. At the Source Awards Liz accidentally fired Tracy Jordan's gun, hitting Steven in the upper thigh while he was trying to get his phone out of her purse. This brought their relationship to an end. Wayne Brady exists in the <i>30 Rock</i> universe independently of Steven Black, having been mentioned on the show, most notably in the season-one episode "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Meets_Dennis" title="Jack Meets Dennis">Jack Meets Dennis</a>" in which Liz remarks that Tracy stole a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Award" title="People's Choice Award">People's Choice Award</a> from him.</li>
<li><b>Jamie Hamilton</b> or "The Coffee Guy" (<a href="/wiki/Val_Emmich" title="Val Emmich">Val Emmich</a>), who only appears in "<a href="/wiki/Cougars_(30_Rock)" title="Cougars (30 Rock)">Cougars</a>," is an attractive younger man who has a crush on Liz Lemon, to whom he delivers coffee. Jamie refers to Liz as the "Sexy Librarian." As the two start to develop feelings for each other, Frank admits that he also has feelings for Jamie. Jamie asks Liz out on a date, but Liz refuses to go due to the difference in their ages. She asks Jamie how old he thinks she is and Jamie guesses 29. Liz quickly lies about her age and agrees that she is definitely 29. Jamie also lies about his age, telling Liz that he's 25, convincing Liz to consider the date. On their date, Liz admits that she's actually 37, whereupon Jamie reveals that he's in fact only 20. Jenna tells Liz that they're <a href="/wiki/Cougar_(slang)" title="Cougar (slang)">cougars</a>. Liz becomes used to the idea of dating a much younger man and agrees to try it out. However, on a subsequent date, she meets Jamie's mother, Beth, who, in addition to sharing her proper forename (Elizabeth), bears a startling resemblance to Liz in looks and dress (indeed, portrayed by Tina Fey's lighting stand-in, Laura Berrios). Seeing Jamie next to Beth, Liz remarks under her breath, "Yup, that's what we look like." She immediately leaves and says "shut it down," ending their relationship.</li>
<li><b>Stewart LaGrange</b> (<a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">Peter Dinklage</a>) is a diplomatic attach√© who works at the United Nations, whom Liz encountered in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Se%C3%B1or_Macho_Solo" title="Se√±or Macho Solo">Se√±or Macho Solo</a>" after rubbing on his head from behind while "baby crazy", having mistaken him for a child due to his <a href="/wiki/Dwarfism" title="Dwarfism">dwarfism</a>. Stewart develops an interest in her due to assuming that her action was an aggressive form of flirting, and takes her out on several dates, while Liz, despite finding him charming, feels mildly uncomfortable due to the circumstances of their meeting. She inadvertently reveals her mistake when she instinctively pulls him back from a fire, offending him greatly. Liz later calls to apologize and suggests a meeting at the Brooklyn Bridge to see if they're willing to try again. However, Liz ends up mistaking a small child for Stewart, who witnesses it and turns away saying "shut it down".</li>
<li><b>Gavin Volure</b> (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Martin" title="Steve Martin">Steve Martin</a>) is a rich entrepreneur and owner of a company called "Sunstream". Volure is agoraphobic, which leaves him confined to his Connecticut estate. Liz becomes interested in a relationship with Gavin when she discovers that his agoraphobia would prevent them from being intimate, something that Liz desires. Gavin later reveals to Liz that he is not agoraphobic, but is really under house arrest for arson, tax fraud, embezzlement and racketeering. Gavin attempts to escape the confines of his home with Liz, but he is captured. Gavin then later attempts a second escape, which succeeds. Gavin runs to <i>TGS</i> where he asks Liz to escape with him to Canada, but Liz refuses. Gavin then climbs to the top of the <i>TGS</i> set with the intention to jump, but, he is stopped by <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Jordan" title="Tracy Jordan">Tracy Jordan</a> and presumably returned to his Connecticut estate.</li>
<li><b>Brad Halster</b> (<a href="/wiki/Roger_Bart" title="Roger Bart">Roger Bart</a>) A consultant and "hatchet man" for NBC, Halster slashes <i>TGS</i>‚Äô budget and staff in "<a href="/wiki/Cutbacks_(30_Rock)" title="Cutbacks (30 Rock)">Cutbacks</a>". Liz attempts to seduce him into restoring her employees' jobs by asking him out on a date and utilizing the show's make-up crew and wardrobe department to maximize her sex appeal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Halster does not reverse his cuts the next morning, and is devastated when an angry Liz causes him to realise the quid-pro-quo nature of the date and moderate petting. Liz's plan ultimately succeeds, however, as Halster's sexual harassment complaint against her necessitates his recusal from consulting on <i>TGS</i>‚Äô budget and Jack Donaghy personally handles evaluating the show. Liz's suspension also gives her a much-needed vacation from work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackie_Jormp-Jomp_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackie_Jormp-Jomp-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>James Franco</b> (<a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">himself</a>) was involved in a mock relationship with Jenna, orchestrated by his publicist in an attempt to quell the rumors of his infatuation with his <a href="/wiki/Dakimakura" title="Dakimakura">Japanese love pillow</a>, Kimiko, in "<a href="/wiki/Klaus_and_Greta" title="Klaus and Greta">Klaus and Greta</a>". The generally sexually repressed Liz uncharacteristically initiates their one-night stand, telling Franco after running into him and Kimiko at a bar, "Let's do this," and repairing to her apartment for their assignation.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jack.27s_love_interests">Jack's love interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Jack's love interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following characters have (at some point during the show) been Jack's girlfriend, wife or fianc√©e.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bianca">Bianca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Bianca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Bianca</b> (<a href="/wiki/Isabella_Rossellini" title="Isabella Rossellini">Isabella Rossellini</a>) is Jack's first wife. Jack's mother disliked her from the beginning and their marriage was troubled. Bianca was introduced in <a href="/wiki/Black_Tie_(30_Rock)" title="Black Tie (30 Rock)">season one, episode twelve</a>. She is engaged to Vincent Foley, and in episode 13 her divorce with Jack was finalized (although they were legally separated since 1989). Jack mentioned that she was too much of a woman for him, which is why they divorced. Bianca tolerated most of Jack's affairs but is jealous of women who can actually make Jack happy, going so far as to violently attack Liz when she pretended to be Jack's fianc√©e.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Black_Tie_(30_Rock)" title="Black Tie (30 Rock)">Black Tie</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Condoleezza_Rice">Condoleezza Rice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Condoleezza Rice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a></div>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a></b> (portrayed by herself) was one of Jack's shorter-lived relationships. Their relationship (and eventual break-up) was alluded to in the episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Break-Up_(30_Rock)" title="The Break-Up (30 Rock)">The Break-Up</a>". Rice later appeared as herself in the <a href="/wiki/30_Rock_(season_5)" title="30 Rock (season 5)">season-five</a> episode "<a href="/wiki/Everything_Sunny_All_the_Time_Always" title="Everything Sunny All the Time Always">Everything Sunny All the Time Always</a>", angry at Jack for apparently ending their relationship with a text message that said "you + me =¬†:(". Among their disagreements concerned her lack of time for him during her tenure as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and whether or not Jack was as talented a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flautist" title="Flautist">flautist</a> as Condoleezza is as a <a href="/wiki/Pianist" title="Pianist">pianist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phoebe">Phoebe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Phoebe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Phoebe</b> (<a href="/wiki/Emily_Mortimer" title="Emily Mortimer">Emily Mortimer</a>) is an art dealer and auctioneer, who works at the <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie's">Christie's</a> branch in <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FilmFloyd_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FilmFloyd-21">[21]</a></sup> She is (supposedly) <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>, claiming to suffer from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertigo_(medical)" title="Vertigo (medical)">vertigo</a> and something called "avian bone syndrome" (which requires that no one touch her). She reintroduces herself to Liz each time they meet, and asserts that her parents were <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FilmFloyd_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-FilmFloyd-21">[21]</a></sup> Jack attracts Phoebe's attention; the two begin dating, and after Liz gave them her blessing Jack quickly asked Phoebe to marry him. She accepts, stunning Liz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FilmFloyd_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-FilmFloyd-21">[21]</a></sup> Jack takes Phoebe to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, later discovering Phoebe is a gold digger. When Liz finds Phoebe holding hands with an older man, Phoebe tells her that he is a former lover. Liz tells her that either she will tell Jack the truth or Liz will; while arguing with Liz, Phoebe drops her <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">English accent</a> and reveals herself as an American. When Liz tells Jack he refuses to believe her, having been warned by Phoebe that Liz was making things up about her. When Jack's mother Colleen appears in "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>", she instantly dislikes Phoebe. When Colleen visits Jack in the hospital, she discovers that Jack's <a href="/wiki/Heart_rate_monitor" title="Heart rate monitor">heart rate monitor</a> functions as a <a href="/wiki/Polygraph" title="Polygraph">polygraph</a>, and asks him whether he is in love with Phoebe. He claims that he is, but the machine indicates he is lying. Phoebe slinks away in defeat; their wedding was subsequently canceled.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Corporate_Crush" title="Corporate Crush">Corporate Crush</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cleveland_(30_Rock)" title="Cleveland (30 Rock)">Cleveland</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="C._C.">C. C.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: C. C.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Celeste "C. C." Cunningham</b> (<a href="/wiki/Edie_Falco" title="Edie Falco">Edie Falco</a>; in-universe by Candace van der Shark (<a href="/wiki/Kristen_Wiig" title="Kristen Wiig">Kristen Wiig</a>) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lifetime_Movie_Network" title="Lifetime Movie Network">Lifetime movie</a>, <i>A Dog Took My Face and Gave Me a Better Face to Change the World: The Celeste Cunningham Story</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congresswoman</a> from <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>. She meets Jack at a cocktail party honoring <a href="/wiki/Robert_Novak" title="Robert Novak">Robert Novak</a>, and the two end up sleeping together. Soon after, Jack discovers her identity and the fact that she is trying to sue NBC's fictitious parent company, Sheinhardt Wig, for dumping Auburn Fantasy Dye #260 into the Chickatagua River (which turned the children of Chickatagua orange). Despite Jack and C.C.'s political conflicts they decide to pursue a relationship (secretly at first), eventually revealing it in Jack's executive dining room. Due to job-related commitments (Jack lives in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and C.C. lives in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>), they decide to break up. She returns in "<a href="/wiki/Cooter_(30_Rock)" title="Cooter (30 Rock)">Cooter</a>", approving the development of a <a href="/wiki/Gay_bomb" title="Gay bomb">gay bomb</a>; this gets Jack fired from his position in Washington, so he can return to 30 Rock (and repays a favor she owed him).</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(30_Rock)" title="Somebody to Love (30 Rock)">Somebody to Love</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Secrets_and_Lies_(30_Rock)" title="Secrets and Lies (30 Rock)">Secrets and Lies</a>", <a href="/wiki/Episode_210" title="Episode 210">Episode 210</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Cooter_(30_Rock)" title="Cooter (30 Rock)">Cooter</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elisa_Pedrera">Elisa Pedrera</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Elisa Pedrera">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Elisa Pedrera</b> (<a href="/wiki/Salma_Hayek" title="Salma Hayek">Salma Hayek</a>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Rican</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurse</a>, who is deeply religious and places a high value on family. She was introduced as a love interest for Jack in season three, when she cared for Colleen (who had injured both hips). While nursing Colleen, Elisa begins a romantic relationship with Jack. She also cares for another patient: an elderly, wheelchair-bound man with <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's disease</a>. Colleen hates Elisa and Jack's relationship; he accuses her of hating every woman with whom he has ever been involved. Elisa's grandmother initially dislikes Jack because he resembles an actor playing a villain on her favorite <i><a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">telenovela</a></i>; she becomes fond of him after Jack has NBC purchase the rights to the show, and changes his doppelg√§nger's part to appeal to elderly women. Although Elisa and Jack had relationship problems on Valentine's Day, they made up (influenced by their love of <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McFlurry" title="McFlurry">McFlurries</a>). In "Larry King", Jack proposes to Elisa. She accepts, informing him that she is going to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and promising to call him. When she returns, Elisa and Jack begin planning their wedding; however, it is revealed that Elisa is notorious among Puerto Ricans for killing her husband after she discovered he was cheating on her. She flies into a homicidal rage when she believes Jack and Liz are having an affair; after being dissuaded she calms down, agreeing with Jack to cancel the wedding and end the relationship because she cannot control her jealousy.</p>
<p>At some point thereafter, while back home in Puerto Rico, Elisa is incarcerated. In "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", Jack convinces Elisa and Nancy Donovan to set aside their devout Catholicism and participate in a <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9nage_%C3%A0_trois" title="M√©nage √† trois">m√©nage √† trois</a> conjugal visit to Elisa's prison, the intensity of which rids both women of their accents.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Se%C3%B1or_Macho_Solo" title="Se√±or Macho Solo">Se√±or Macho Solo</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flu_Shot_(30_Rock)" title="Flu Shot (30 Rock)">Flu Shot</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Generalissimo_(30_Rock)" title="Generalissimo (30 Rock)">Generalissimo</a>", "<a href="/wiki/St._Valentine%27s_Day_(30_Rock)" title="St. Valentine's Day (30 Rock)">St. Valentine's Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Larry_King_(30_Rock)" title="Larry King (30 Rock)">Larry King</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Ones_(30_Rock)" title="The Ones (30 Rock)">The Ones</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nancy_Donovan">Nancy Donovan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Nancy Donovan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Nancy Donovan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Julianne_Moore" title="Julianne Moore">Julianne Moore</a>; in-universe by <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Nixon" title="Cynthia Nixon">Cynthia Nixon</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>"), was Jack's high-school crush, a devout Catholic with a pronounced Boston accent. She is married with two sons, though it is clear her marriage is unfulfilling. She and Jack were in the same German class (where Jack was called "Klaus" and Nancy "Greta"); Nancy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voice-mail" title="Voice-mail">voice-mail</a> code stands for "Klaus", indicating that Nancy has feelings for him. By the time Nancy decides to divorce her husband, Jack is already involved with Avery. He dates both women, unable to decide. Nancy meets Avery and finds out she is pregnant, which Nancy tells Jack before leaving. She is played by <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Nixon" title="Cynthia Nixon">Cynthia Nixon</a> in the TV-movie made about Avery, <i><a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a></i>. In "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", Jack reconnects with Nancy and Elisa Pedrera, convincing both women to set aside their devout Catholicism and participate in a <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9nage_%C3%A0_trois" title="M√©nage √† trois">m√©nage √† trois</a> conjugal visit to Elisa's prison, the intensity of which rids both women of their accents. <i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Santa_(30_Rock)" title="Secret Santa (30 Rock)">Secret Santa</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Winter_Madness" title="Winter Madness">Winter Madness</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Lee_Marvin_vs._Derek_Jeter" title="Lee Marvin vs. Derek Jeter">Lee Marvin vs. Derek Jeter</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avery_Jessup-Donaghy">Avery Jessup-Donaghy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Avery Jessup-Donaghy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Avery Jessup</b> (<a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Banks" title="Elizabeth Banks">Elizabeth Banks</a>; in-universe by <a href="/wiki/Jenna_Maroney" title="Jenna Maroney">Jenna Maroney</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jane_Krakowski" title="Jane Krakowski">Jane Krakowski</a>) in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a></i>) is Jack's second wife. Jessup is a conservative media personality and the host of political talk-show <i>The Hot-Box</i> and commentator on <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a>. She begins their relationship after a one-night stand during season four, after Jack is convinced that Nancy will never leave her husband. He dates both simultaneously, and later chooses Avery over Nancy after being told by Nancy that Avery is pregnant. Of <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedish</a> descent from <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, she attended <a href="/wiki/Choate_Rosemary_Hall" title="Choate Rosemary Hall">Choate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>. They (supposedly) marry during season five, between "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Mrs._Donaghy" title="Mrs. Donaghy">Mrs. Donaghy</a>"; however, Avery does not know that the officiant married Jack and Liz (the problem was fixed offscreen). She gave birth to Jack's daughter during "<a href="/wiki/Double-Edged_Sword_(30_Rock)" title="Double-Edged Sword (30 Rock)">Double-Edged Sword</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> (making her Canadian-American), and named her Elizabeth Donaghy after Liz Lemon (nicknamed "Liddy" in honor of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Dole" title="Elizabeth Dole">"Liddy" Dole</a>, <a href="/wiki/G._Gordon_Liddy" title="G. Gordon Liddy">G. Gordon Liddy</a> and Jack's martial-arts instructor, Li Di.). In "<a href="/wiki/Everything_Sunny_All_the_Time_Always" title="Everything Sunny All the Time Always">Everything Sunny All the Time Always</a>", Avery is on a trip described by Jack as "a hot-blondes-in-weird-places initiative" by <a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC News</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. However, things do not go well; she is detained in <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> by <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a>, and forced to participate in an unrealistic propaganda video as a Western journalist reporting how the free world is being conquered by North Korea. Despite Jack's attempts to get her back (with getting help from his ex, <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a>) she is stranded in Korea and <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forcibly married</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-un" title="Kim Jong-un">Kim Jong-un</a>. Jack had a hard time dealing with her absence, as well as his intense feelings for her mother Diana. She was rescued from North Korea towards the end of the sixth season in the episode "The Return of Avery Jessup". Shortly after Avery's return, Jack discovers that Avery has fallen in love with another detained reporter, and the couple divorce at the altar while trying to renew their vows in the last episode of season 6.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Anna_Howard_Shaw_Day" title="Anna Howard Shaw Day">Anna Howard Shaw Day</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Future_Husband" title="Future Husband">Future Husband</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Lee_Marvin_vs._Derek_Jeter" title="Lee Marvin vs. Derek Jeter">Lee Marvin vs. Derek Jeter</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/When_it_Rains,_it_Pours_(30_Rock)" title="When it Rains, it Pours (30 Rock)">When it Rains, it Pours</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Gentleman%27s_Intermission" title="Gentleman's Intermission">Gentleman's Intermission</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>", "<a href="/wiki/%C2%A1Qu%C3%A9_Sorpresa!" title="¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!">¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Double-Edged_Sword_(30_Rock)" title="Double-Edged Sword (30 Rock)">Double-Edged Sword</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Everything_Sunny_All_the_Time_Always" title="Everything Sunny All the Time Always">Everything Sunny All the Time Always</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_Avery_Jessup" title="The Return of Avery Jessup">The Return of Avery Jessup</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_characters.27_relatives"><span id="Main_characters.27_family"></span>Main characters' relatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Main characters' relatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dick_Lemon">Dick Lemon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Dick Lemon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Dick Lemon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Buck_Henry" title="Buck Henry">Buck Henry</a>; <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_Chastain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sheffield Chastain (page does not exist)">Sheffield Chastain</a> as young Dick) is the father of Liz and Mitch Lemon. Like Liz, he grew up in <a href="/wiki/White_Haven,_Pennsylvania" title="White Haven, Pennsylvania">White Haven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, where he still lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Liz mentions that he served at Pearl Harbor, although quickly reveals this was during the Korean War. Outwardly supportive of Liz, Dick disagrees with, and is embarrassed by, many of her decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ludachristmas_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ludachristmas-27">[27]</a></sup> At one point he arrives in New York declaring that he and his wife are "on a break" and he even accidentally tries to hit on Liz in a dark nightclub. Unknown to Liz, Dick once made out with Jenna on New Years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Appears in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Gentleman%27s_Intermission" title="Gentleman's Intermission">Gentleman's Intermission</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Margaret_Lemon">Margaret Lemon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Margaret Lemon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Margaret Lemon</b> (n√©e Freeman) (<a href="/wiki/Anita_Gillette" title="Anita Gillette">Anita Gillette</a>; uncredited actress in "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>"; <a href="/wiki/Tina_Fey" title="Tina Fey">Tina Fey</a> as a teen in "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>") is Liz's mother. Born <i>circa</i> 1937,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> she "repeatedly lost her virginity" at or about the age of 15<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> to the love of her life, <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">Buzz Aldrin</a> (whom she called "Ed" because there were already five "Buzzes" in Montclair), while Waldo the town perv watched from the bushes. After she graduated from secretary school and Ed was joining the astronaut program in 1963, he asked her to marry him, but Margaret had just started a job with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sterling_Cooper" title="Sterling Cooper">Sterling Cooper</a> and did not feel she could just pick up and leave, being an "old maid" of 26. Accordingly, she later settled for <a href="#Dick_Lemon">Dick Lemon</a> and bore him two children: Mitch Lemon and Elizabeth M. "Liz" Lemon. She still believes computers to be the size of rooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Moms_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Moms-31">[31]</a></sup> Like Dick, Margaret expresses support for Liz but quietly disagrees with many of her decisions and opinions. She attempts to disabuse Liz of the belief in a "Mr. Right" and encourages her to settle as she did. Dr. Aldrin, meanwhile, is grateful to not have put Margaret through his years of alcoholism and depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Moms_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Moms-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Appears in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terry_and_Janet">Terry and Janet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Terry and Janet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Terry</b> and <b>Janet</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dante_Hoagland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dante Hoagland (page does not exist)">Dante Hoagland</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Remy_Bond&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Remy Bond (page does not exist)">Remy Bond</a>) are fraternal twins whom Liz and Criss adopt in "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>". In addition to their genders, races, and names, their personalities are immediately revealed to be nearly identical to those of, respectively, Tracy and Jenna. Upon meeting them at the airport, Liz muses happily that gaining miniature versions of her two 'problem children' just as <i>TGS</i> is cancelled "seems about right" and she embraces the pair.</p>
<p>Their bedrooms are on second story of the family's condominium, Apartment 3B, 160 <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Drive_(Manhattan)" title="Riverside Drive (Manhattan)">Riverside Drive</a>, Liz having purchased the two apartments with her <i>Dealbreakers</i> earnings in "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>", and Criss having performed much of the work to renovate the former Apartment 4B into their second floor. Unlike her new mother who is obsessed with not exposing her feet, Janet has to be reminded in "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>" to put on her shoes and socks before school.</p>
<p>The pair accompany their mother to her work on <i>Grizz &amp; Herz</i> at least once, as shown in "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>"‚Äîpossibly on Take Your Black Kid to Work Day, which would place the scene on a Wednesday (per Sue in "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>"). After a year in the Lemon-Chros family, Terry and Janet appear to have become less like Tracy and Jenna; they are well-behaved on-set, sitting quietly off-camera and studying their homework while their mother and Dot Com produce the show.</p>
