<p>Despite the pair having not joined the family until well into their childhood, Terry (if not Janet as well) is implied to have eventually taken their new mother's (not their new father's) surname, as Liz's mixed-race great-granddaughter is named Eliza Lemon in "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>".</p>
<p><i>Appear in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eliza_Lemon">Eliza Lemon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Eliza Lemon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Eliza Lemon</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Barrett_Doss&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Barrett Doss (page does not exist)">Barrett Doss</a>) is Liz's African-American great-granddaughter. She appears only fleetingly in a single scene, but is revealed to be indispensable to the series. Growing up, Eliza hears the stories Liz would tell about her days at <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>. As an adult in the early <a href="/wiki/22nd_century" title="22nd century">22nd century</a>, she develops a sitcom based on those stories, which she pitches to NBC's receptive (and strangely immortal and ageless) president, Kenneth Parcell, while flying cars zoom through the sky past his office window. Kenneth only addresses her as "Ms. Lemon" (as he did her ancestor, and which conveniently rhymes with <i>Liz</i> Lemon); her forename is given in the closing credits before her scene.</p>
<p>The sequence is an homage to <i><a href="/wiki/St._Elsewhere" title="St. Elsewhere">St. Elsewhere</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s famous <a href="/wiki/St._Elsewhere#.22The_Last_One.22" title="St. Elsewhere">closing scene</a> - complete with a model of the series' namesake building within a snow globe stared at by a mentally challenged male - and implies that the series <i>30 Rock</i> had been a <a href="/wiki/Historical_period_drama" title="Historical period drama">period piece</a> of Eliza's creation in the distant future, as <i>St. Elsewhere</i> had all been a daydream in <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Westphall" title="Tommy Westphall">Tommy Westphall</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autistic</a> imagination.</p>
<p><i>Appears in</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Last_Lunch" title="Last Lunch">Last Lunch</a>"</p>
<p><span id="Paul_Lastname"></span></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paul_L.27astnam.C3.A9_.28Mr._Jenna_Maroney.29">Paul L'astnam√© (Mr. Jenna Maroney)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Paul L'astnam√© (Mr. Jenna Maroney)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3654" data-file-width="2487" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG/170px-Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG/255px-Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG/340px-Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Will_Forte_2011_Shankbone.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Will Forte portrays Paul L'astnam√©, Jenna's fianc√©</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Mr. Jenna Maroney</b>, formerly known as <b>Paul L'astnam√©</b> (<a href="/wiki/Will_Forte" title="Will Forte">Will Forte</a>), is Jenna's boyfriend and later husband. He is a female-impersonator (most often dressed as Jenna) who often refers to himself as a "she-man" or "shman." Paul and Jenna first met when Paul won first place in a Jenna Maroney impersonator contest in which Jenna herself placed fourth (a parody of an urban legend about <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a>, who allegedly finished fourth in a Charlie Chaplin contest) and Jenna realized that by dating Paul she could date herself. They began a relationship characterized by many unconventional sexual practices. The pair become engaged to marry when he crashes a <i>TGS</i> sketch in "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>". In "<a href="/wiki/My_Whole_Life_Is_Thunder" title="My Whole Life Is Thunder">My Whole Life Is Thunder</a>", Jenna and Paul are married in a surprise ceremony at the funeral of Jack's mother. Paul takes Jenna's first and last names.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Argus_(30_Rock)" title="Argus (30 Rock)">Argus</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Chain_Reaction_of_Mental_Anguish" title="Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish">Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Respawn_(30_Rock)" title="Respawn (30 Rock)">Respawn</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Tuxedo_Begins" title="The Tuxedo Begins">The Tuxedo Begins</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woggels!" title="Meet the Woggels!">Meet the Woggels!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Murphy_Brown_Lied_to_Us" title="Murphy Brown Lied to Us">Murphy Brown Lied to Us</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", "<a href="/wiki/My_Whole_Life_Is_Thunder" title="My Whole Life Is Thunder">My Whole Life Is Thunder</a>." Forte had previously appeared in <i>30 Rock</i> as Tomas, a servant of Prince Gerhardt, in the season one episode "<a href="/wiki/Black_Tie_(30_Rock)" title="Black Tie (30 Rock)">Black Tie</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angie_Jordan">Angie Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Angie Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sherri_Shepherd.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="501" data-file-width="376" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sherri_Shepherd.jpg/170px-Sherri_Shepherd.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sherri_Shepherd.jpg/255px-Sherri_Shepherd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Sherri_Shepherd.jpg/340px-Sherri_Shepherd.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sherri_Shepherd.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sherri Shepherd portrays Angie Jordan, Tracy's wife</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Angie Jordan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Sherri_Shepherd" title="Sherri Shepherd">Sherri Shepherd</a>‚Äî<a href="/wiki/Sharon_Wilkins" title="Sharon Wilkins">Sharon Wilkins</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Writer" title="Jack the Writer">Jack the Writer</a>") has been <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Jordan" title="Tracy Jordan">Tracy Jordan</a>'s wife since August 30, 1991. They enjoy odd forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_roleplaying" title="Sexual roleplaying">sexual roleplaying</a>. Tracy implied in "<a href="/wiki/Black_Tie_(30_Rock)" title="Black Tie (30 Rock)">Black Tie</a>" that he and Angie have an <a href="/wiki/Open_marriage" title="Open marriage">open marriage</a>, but Angie is less than happy with her husband's extramarital escapades (which are later revealed as stories to boost Tracy's image). She threw Tracy out of their house in "<a href="/wiki/SeinfeldVision" title="SeinfeldVision">SeinfeldVision</a>", reconciling with him in "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>". A domineering, bombastic person, she is demanding of her husband (financially and sexually). It is revealed in <a href="/wiki/The_Ones" title="The Ones">The Ones</a> that Tracy has actually never cheated on his wife, and that his supposed "affairs" are all for show. Like Tracy, Angie addresses Liz by her full name. She is rude to Liz, nearly attacking her (after Liz stops trying to appease her) and ordering her off the set. In "Mrs. Donaghy" Angie stars in her own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_channel)" title="Bravo (US TV channel)">Bravo</a> reality program, <i>Queen of Jordan</i> (which figured prominently during the rest of season five, due to Tracy Morgan's <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan#Health_problems" title="Tracy Morgan">medical leave</a>).</p>
<p>For her initial appearance in "<a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Writer" title="Jack the Writer">Jack the Writer</a>" (a non-speaking <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a>), she was played by <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Wilkins" title="Sharon Wilkins">Sharon Wilkins</a>. In all subsequent episodes (beginning with "Up All Night"), she is portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Sherri_Shepherd" title="Sherri Shepherd">Sherri Shepherd</a> and has a more substantial role.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(30_Rock)" title="Up All Night (30 Rock)">Up All Night</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Collection_(30_Rock)" title="The Collection (30 Rock)">The Collection</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senor_Macho_Solo" title="Senor Macho Solo">Senor Macho Solo</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show#0001" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show#0001</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mrs._Donaghy" title="Mrs. Donaghy">Mrs. Donaghy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan_(30_Rock)" title="Queen of Jordan (30 Rock)">Queen of Jordan</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan_2:_Mystery_of_the_Phantom_Pooper" title="Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper">Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleen_Donaghy">Colleen Donaghy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Colleen Donaghy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg/170px-Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg/255px-Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg/340px-Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elaine_Stritch_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elaine Stritch portrays Colleen Donaghy, Jack's mother</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Colleen Donaghy (n√©e Murphy)</b> (<a href="/wiki/Elaine_Stritch" title="Elaine Stritch">Elaine Stritch</a>) is Jack's overbearing, demanding mother who lives in a <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> retirement home. According to Jack, the Murphy family are "a bunch of mud farmers and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bestiality" title="Bestiality">sheep rapists</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> He appears as if he wants nothing to do with her although deep down, he loves her. Colleen first appeared in season 1, episode 21; she is critical of Jack's abilities, and hesitant to show him affection. In season 3, episode 20, Colleen reveals that her ex-husband (Jim Donaghy) left her in 1957 and returned in 1959. Jack was conceived in 1958 during Colleen's affair with <a href="#Milton_Greene">Milton Greene</a>.</p>
<p>Colleen has nagged Jack his whole life,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> even blaming him for <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination" title="John F. Kennedy assassination">death</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-episode_Christmas_Special_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-episode_Christmas_Special-34">[34]</a></sup> and for his father leaving. When Jack's collie, Pop, was accidentally run over by the postman, Colleen left him to die in the street. She even tried to send Jack to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam</a> when he was 12 years old in order to make a man out of him. Colleen embarrassed him by having him play "<a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">The Star-Spangled Banner</a>" on his flute in front of his hockey team.</p>
<p>Colleen's cold and stern demeanor is contrasted by her behavior at Christmas. After Jim abandoned the family, Colleen would acquire mountains of toys for her children each Christmas, despite the family's poverty, by in exchange for providing sexual favors to the [fictional] <a href="/wiki/FAO_Schwarz" title="FAO Schwarz">Frederick August Otto Schwarz, III</a>. Unaware of the transaction, Jack resented his mother hosting Mr. Schwartz and her infidelity toward his father. Colleen additionally gave her children unique Christmas traditions and fables that Jack assumed were standard holiday practice, such as Mrs. Claus hanging the children's stockings. He is in his 50s when Liz Lemon causes him to realize the truth and gain a new appreciation and love for his mother and her holiday practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-episode_Christmas_Special_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-episode_Christmas_Special-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite rarely having a good thing to say about anyone, Colleen takes an instant liking to Liz, mistaking her for Jack's actual fianc√©e, <a href="#Phoebe">Phoebe</a>. When he tells her that it isn't Liz whom he was marrying, Colleen's response is "Why the hell not?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiatus_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hiatus-35">[35]</a></sup> It is during a heart-attack-causing argument with Colleen that Jack realizes that he does not love Phoebe, and calls off the engagement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiatus_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hiatus-35">[35]</a></sup> No indication is made that Colleen is aware of the later <a href="#Liz_Donaghy">temporary accidental marriage of Jack and Liz</a>. Although fond of Liz, Colleen nevertheless delights in manipulating the Lemons into a resentment-fueled argument between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ludachristmas_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ludachristmas-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colleen dies of a heart attack in "<a href="/wiki/My_Whole_Life_Is_Thunder" title="My Whole Life Is Thunder">My Whole Life Is Thunder</a>" during a visit to New York to spend time with Jack, attempting to guilt him and seemingly depriving him of her approval literally up to her last breath. Her last words to Jack are "I just want you to be happy," which Jack hears as "I just want you to be 'happy'" and takes as sarcasm and "one last twist of the knife." Jack and Liz subsequently discover in "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>" that Colleen spent her final years in a cohabitational lesbian relationship and - much more shockingly - was happy and well-liked in the couple's retirement community, where she was seen as kind and loving. Jack is sent into a tailspin by the revelation that his mother actually wanted him to be happy, which leads to him re-evaluating his life and career in the finale.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Special_(30_Rock)" title="Christmas Special (30 Rock)">Christmas Special</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Natural_Order" title="The Natural Order">The Natural Order</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woggels!" title="Meet the Woggels!">Meet the Woggels!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/My_Whole_Life_Is_Thunder" title="My Whole Life Is Thunder">My Whole Life Is Thunder</a>", and in still photographs in "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milton_Greene">Milton Greene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Milton Greene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1805" data-file-width="1200" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg/170px-Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg/255px-Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg/340px-Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alan_Alda_by_Bridget_Laudien.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alan Alda portrays Milton Greene, Jack's biological father</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Milton Greene</b> (<a href="/wiki/Alan_Alda" title="Alan Alda">Alan Alda</a>) is Jack's biological father. Milton rented a room from Colleen Donaghy in the Boston suburb of Sadchester in 1958, during one of Jimmy Donaghy's numerous abandonments of his family. The two soon engaged in coitus and, unbeknownst to Milton, begat Jack Donaghy.</p>
<p>A half-century later, Milton is a liberal professor at <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bennington_College" title="Bennington College">Bennington College</a>. In the interim, Milton had married and sired a son whom he and the child's mother refused to name, opining that children should chose their own names; Spider-Man Greene is Jack's unsuspecting half-brother. A fan of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> (much to Jack's bemusement), Milton is writing a multi-volume biography of the former President, entitled <i>From Peanut to President</i>; <a href="/wiki/Betty_White" title="Betty White">Betty White</a> is reading a volume when Tracy Jordan telephones her in "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Mountain_(30_Rock)" title="Stone Mountain (30 Rock)">Stone Mountain</a>".</p>
<p>Jack discovers in "<a href="/wiki/The_Natural_Order" title="The Natural Order">The Natural Order</a>" that Jimmy Donaghy had been gone when Jack was conceived. He and Lenny Wozniak narrow his possible fathers down to three men whom Jack lures to Manhattan under false pretences in "<a href="/wiki/Mamma_Mia_(30_Rock)" title="Mamma Mia (30 Rock)">Mamma Mia</a>". Seeing that George Park is <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">Korean</a> and then learning that Fred O'Dwyer lost his genitals in a grenade explosion during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Jack invites Milton to his office and reveals their relation. Milton is overjoyed and announces that he is in need of a kidney to survive. In "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>", Jack is relieved to learn that he is not a match and decides to hold a charity concert to find a kidney for Milton. It is revealed in "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>" that <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Costello" title="Elvis Costello">Elvis Costello</a> was a tissue match and donated a kidney to Milton.</p>
<p>Milton's liberalism is exaggerated as a foil to Jack's conservative politics. He is kind, enthusiastic, and supportive of Jack.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Mamma_Mia_(30_Rock)" title="Mamma Mia (30 Rock)">Mamma Mia</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Attack_Zone" title="Christmas Attack Zone">Christmas Attack Zone</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tracy_Jr..2C_George_Foreman_and_Virginia_Jordan">Tracy Jr., George Foreman and Virginia Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Tracy Jr., George Foreman and Virginia Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Tracy Jordan Jr.</b> (<a href="/wiki/Bobb%27e_J._Thompson" title="Bobb'e J. Thompson">Bobb'e J. Thompson</a>) is the combative son of Tracy and Angie Jordan. The Jordans have another son, <b>George Foreman Jordan</b>, who appeared in "Gavin Volure" and "The Bubble" (played by Jalani McNair), and had his first speaking role in the season 6 episode "Meet the Woggels!", where he was accepted into <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> (to Tracy's disapproval) and played by Dante E. Clark. The Jordans' daughter <b>Virginia</b> was born in "<a href="/wiki/When_It_Rains,_It_Pours_(30_Rock)" title="When It Rains, It Pours (30 Rock)">When It Rains, It Pours</a>," and appears twice in the 6th and 7th Season, played by twin infants Zoya and Zuri Bacai.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Gavin_Volure" title="Gavin Volure">Gavin Volure</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Funcooker" title="The Funcooker">The Funcooker</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Bubble_(30_Rock)" title="The Bubble (30 Rock)">The Bubble</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>" (Tracy Jr.), "Gavin Volure", "The Bubble", "<a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woggels!" title="Meet the Woggels!">Meet the Woggels!</a>" (George Foreman), "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan_2:_Mystery_of_the_Phantom_Pooper" title="Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper">Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Aunt_Phatso_vs._Jack_Donaghy" title="Aunt Phatso vs. Jack Donaghy">Aunt Phatso vs. Jack Donaghy</a>" (Virginia)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verna_Maroney">Verna Maroney</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Verna Maroney">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Verna Maroney</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jan_Hooks" title="Jan Hooks">Jan Hooks</a>) is Jenna's mother. A quintessential <a href="/wiki/Stage_mother" title="Stage mother">stage mother</a>, she spent Jenna's childhood forcing her to perform in beauty pagents and talent shows, and is responsible for Jenna's need for the spotlight and for many of her neuroses. After a lengthy period of estrangement, she reappears in Jenna's life in the show's fourth season, and initially appears intent on making amends with her daughter. This is revealed to be a ploy: Verna has manipulated Jenna into forgiving her so she can pitch a reality show to Jack. Jack bribes Verna to pretend to be a caring mother; the act works, thrilling Jenna. As a running gag, Jenna and Verna have a habit of singing incestuously inappropriate duets.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Verna_(30_Rock)" title="Verna (30 Rock)">Verna</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diana_Jessup">Diana Jessup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Diana Jessup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1867" data-file-width="1412" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg/170px-MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg/255px-MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg/340px-MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MarySteenburgenDec09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mary Steenburgen portrays Diana Jessup, Avery's mother</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Diana Jessup</b> (<a href="/wiki/Mary_Steenburgen" title="Mary Steenburgen">Mary Steenburgen</a>) is Avery's mother and Jack's mother-in-law. Diana shares many of the same qualities with her daughter, which makes Jack instantly attracted to her. Diana is also extremely attracted to Jack. The two end up kissing at the opening of a fake Russian restaurant, but Liz covers for them, lying that Jack kisses everyone when he greets them. When Avery returns, Jack admits to Avery that he kissed Diana, but Avery forgives him, however, it is shown that there still is some tension between Avery and Diana due to the kiss. Despite their distant relationship, Diana truly loves and cares for her daughter, evidenced by her getting the United Nations involved in Avery's rescue, and her overseeing the making of a television film about Avery to make sure that the film portrays her daughter in a favorable light.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan_2:_Mystery_of_the_Phantom_Pooper" title="Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper">Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_Will_Happen_to_the_Gang_Next_Year%3F" title="What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?">What Will Happen to the Gang Next Year?</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sylvia_Rossitano">Sylvia Rossitano</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Sylvia Rossitano">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Sylvia Rossitano</b> (<a href="/wiki/Patti_LuPone" title="Patti LuPone">Patti LuPone</a>) is Frank's mother. Sylvia is a stereotypical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian-American" title="Italian-American">Italian-American</a> mother, extremely loving towards her son, but also incredibly overbearing. Sylvia is also an incredible cook. Sylvia's husband was a lawyer for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Mafia" title="Italian Mafia">Italian Mafia</a>, until he had to go into hiding in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>. Sylvia lied to her son about this, telling him instead that his father abandoned him. Sylvia believes it important that Frank find a wife, but she disapproves heavily of her son's relationship with his high-school teacher Lynn Onkman (<a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>). Sylvia ultimately accepts Frank and Lynn's relationship after Sylvia sees Lynn's passion towards Frank. In a nod to LuPone's singing career, Sylvia is portrayed as being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tone_deaf" title="Tone deaf">tone deaf</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>".</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Goodbye,_My_Friend" title="Goodbye, My Friend">Goodbye, My Friend</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Moms" title="The Moms">The Moms</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Alexis_Goodlooking_and_the_Case_of_the_Missing_Whisky" title="Alexis Goodlooking and the Case of the Missing Whisky">Alexis Goodlooking and the Case of the Missing Whisky</a>".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_characters"><span id="Other_recurring_characters"></span>Recurring characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Recurring characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leo_Spaceman">Leo Spaceman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Leo Spaceman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2664" data-file-width="1456" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/170px-Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/255px-Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/340px-Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chris_Parnell_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chris Parnell portrays Leo Spaceman</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>"Dr." Leo Spaceman</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/…ô/ 'a' in 'about'">…ô</span><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="/t É/ 'ch' in 'china'">t É</span><span title="/…õ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">…õ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/…™/ or /…ô/ 'e' in 'roses'">·µª</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>sp…ô-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">CHEM</span></span></b>-…ôn</i></a></span>‚Äîexcept by Tracy, who pronounces his name like the English word "<a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">spaceman</a>") (<a href="/wiki/Chris_Parnell" title="Chris Parnell">Chris Parnell</a>) is a graduate of the <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City_Medicine_and_Pharmacy_University" title="Ho Chi Minh City Medicine and Pharmacy University">Ho Chi Minh City School of Medicine</a>. He is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quack_doctor" title="Quack doctor">quack doctor</a> who practices questionable medicine, such as giving a "medical professional's seal of approval" to a defective "meat machine," and as such is legally required to put quotation marks around his title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Despite his obvious shortcomings, Jack is unwavering in his support of Spaceman's "skills". He wrote a bestselling book, <i>The Cigarette Diet</i>, and found shocking medical abnormalities during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desert_Storm" title="Desert Storm">Desert Storm</a> which his boss refused to report to <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>. At one time Spaceman dated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lynette_%22Squeaky%22_Fromme" title='Lynette "Squeaky" Fromme'>Lynette "Squeaky" Fromme</a>, whom he described as "difficult". Leo has been portrayed as a classic "quack", doing and saying very weird things. For instance, when <a href="/wiki/Jack_Donaghy" title="Jack Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</a> visits him for a checkup in "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>," Spaceman instructs Jack to cough several times while seeming to examine him below the frame (implying a <a href="/wiki/Hernia" title="Hernia">hernia</a> inspection), but afterward says, "Okay, let's start the examination." In his last appearance on the series, he is appointed <a href="/wiki/Surgeon_General_of_the_United_States" title="Surgeon General of the United States">Surgeon General of the United States</a>, and breaks the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_wall" title="Fourth wall">fourth wall</a> by saying "That's a series wrap on Leo Spaceman, suckers!".</p>
<p>Leo is the son of Dr. Harold (a/k/a Heinrich) Spaceman, an equally incompetent and unethical physician. After serving in World War II, the elder Dr. Spaceman left Germany for a new life in the United States. In the 1950s, he was a television spokesman for Chatterton cigarettes, promoting their tar and nicotine to expectant mothers, as being necessary for their babies' skeletal development. In addition to his Nazi past, he was a notorious paedophile. "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>"</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Tracy_Does_Conan" title="Tracy Does Conan">Tracy Does Conan</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Rural_Juror" title="The Rural Juror">The Rural Juror</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fireworks_(30_Rock)" title="Fireworks (30 Rock)">Fireworks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(30_Rock)" title="Hiatus (30 Rock)">Hiatus</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Gets_in_the_Game" title="Jack Gets in the Game">Jack Gets in the Game</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Succession_(30_Rock)" title="Succession (30 Rock)">Succession</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flu_Shot_(30_Rock)" title="Flu Shot (30 Rock)">Flu Shot</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Retreat_to_Move_Forward" title="Retreat to Move Forward">Retreat to Move Forward</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Funcooker" title="The Funcooker">The Funcooker</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sun_Tea_(30_Rock)" title="Sun Tea (30 Rock)">Sun Tea</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dealbreakers_Talk_Show#0001" title="Dealbreakers Talk Show">Dealbreakers Talk Show#0001</a>", "<a href="/wiki/When_It_Rains,_It_Pours_(30_Rock)" title="When It Rains, It Pours (30 Rock)">When It Rains, It Pours</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mrs._Donaghy" title="Mrs. Donaghy">Mrs. Donaghy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Respawn_(30_Rock)" title="Respawn (30 Rock)">Respawn</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Nothing_Left_to_Lose_(30_Rock)" title="Nothing Left to Lose (30 Rock)">Nothing Left to Lose</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mazel_Tov,_Dummies!" title="Mazel Tov, Dummies!">Mazel Tov, Dummies!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>", <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Pepper" title="Dr. Pepper">Dr. Pepper</a> commercials.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lenny_Wosniak">Lenny Wosniak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Lenny Wosniak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3133" data-file-width="2090" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg/170px-Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg/255px-Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg/340px-Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steve_Buscemi_2009_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Steve Buscemi portrays Lenny Wosniak</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Lenny Wosniak</b> (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Buscemi" title="Steve Buscemi">Steve Buscemi</a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_investigator" title="Private investigator">private investigator</a> occasionally hired by Jack. He first appears in the second-season episode "The Collection", where (while spying on Jack to determine if he has any skeletons in his closet which could prevent him from being named the new CEO of General Electric) he discovers Jack has a large collection of homemade cookie jars. Jack also hires him in the third season to obtain personal information about a man his mother was seeing, and (later) the true identity of his father. In "<a href="/wiki/The_Tuxedo_Begins" title="The Tuxedo Begins">The Tuxedo Begins</a>", Jack hires him after he is mugged. During his investigations, Wosniak will occasionally don a disguise as he sees fit. He claims he was once "part of a special task force of very young-looking cops who infiltrated high schools," in a reference to <i><a href="/wiki/21_Jump_Street" title="21 Jump Street">21 Jump Street</a>.</i> While attempting to infiltrate the pages union by seducing Kenneth, Wosniak affixes a blond wig in order to assume the persona of the "nympho-coed Charlene LaRue"- the attempt ultimately fails as Kenneth was "impervious" to Mrs. LaRue's charms. In "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>" Lenny goes undercover at Kaylee Hooper's high school as a female drama teacher, Jan Foster, discovers that he prefers being Jan to being Lenny, and gets engaged to a female math teacher.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/The_Collection_(30_Rock)" title="The Collection (30 Rock)">The Collection</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Natural_Order" title="The Natural Order">The Natural Order</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mamma_Mia_(30_Rock)" title="Mamma Mia (30 Rock)">Mamma Mia</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Season_4_(30_Rock)" title="Season 4 (30 Rock)">Season 4</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Tuxedo_Begins" title="The Tuxedo Begins">The Tuxedo Begins</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shawn_Connelly">Shawn Connelly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Shawn Connelly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Shawn Connelly</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seth_Kirschner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seth Kirschner (page does not exist)">Seth Kirschner</a>) directs Tracy Jordan in <i>Garfield 3: Feline Groovy</i> until Tracy abruptly quits and causes the production to be shut down. His career ruined, Shawn is forced to move back into his parents' home. He again finds himself directing Tracy in an advertisement for the Boys &amp; Girls Clubs, each elaborate take of which is ruined by Tracy's incompetence, until Jack Donaghy arrives on-set, feeds Tracy a mouth-full of jelly beans, and imitates his voice. Jack twice hires Shawn to direct films he executive produces and which star Jenna Maroney. The first is the <a href="/wiki/Philip_Rosenthal" title="Philip Rosenthal">Phil Rosenthal</a>-penned family-friendly horror-torture soft-core porn film, <i>Take My Hand</i> promoting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanford,_Connecticut" title="Stanford, Connecticut">Stamford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>. He follows that up with the docudrama Liz Lemon wrote about Jack's wife's North Korean abduction: <i>Kidnapped by Danger: The Avery Jessup Story, brought to you with limited interruptions by Pride bladder control pads. Pride: make every room a bathroom</i>. Shawn discovers Jenna Maroney to be just as horrible to deal with as Tracy was, when he tries to direct her in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order:_Special_Victims_Unit" title="Law &amp; Order: Special Victims Unit">Law &amp; Order: Special Victims Unit</a></i> after <i>TGS</i> is cancelled.</p>
<p><i>Appears In:</i> "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Crevasse" title="Into the Crevasse">Into the Crevasse</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Emanuelle_Goes_to_Dinosaur_Land" title="Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land">Emanuelle Goes to Dinosaur Land</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Reaganing" title="Reaganing">Reaganing</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Heart_Connecticut" title="I Heart Connecticut">I Heart Connecticut</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_by_Danger" title="Kidnapped by Danger">Kidnapped by Danger</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hogcock!" title="Hogcock!">Hogcock!</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bev">Bev</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Bev">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Bev</b> (<a href="/wiki/Megan_Mullally" title="Megan Mullally">Megan Mullally</a>) is Liz Lemon's (later, Liz &amp; Criss Chros') adoption agent. She initially intends to reject Liz at the conclusion of her evaluation visit to Liz's workplace, many of the interviews of Liz's co-workers having reflected badly upon Liz or the safety of the studio for a child. Before Bev files her report, however, she sustains a head injury and forgets that she has conducted the evaluation. Liz gets the crew to help her "do over" the evaluation, hoping for a better result.</p>
<p>Although Liz's marriage to Criss was calculated to increase her chance at adopting, Bev explains that there remains a four-year waiting list for newborns and tries to convince Liz to adopt an older child. Liz eventually agrees after realising that years of dealing with her "problem children" Tracy and Jenna have proven her parenting skills. Bev subsequently convinces Liz to accept twins rather than a single child and schedules their arrival for a few short days later. She gets the date wrong, however, and informs Criss that Terry and Janet are flying in that afternoon.</p>
<p><i>Appears In:</i> "<a href="/wiki/Do-Over" title="Do-Over">Do-Over</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(30_Rock)" title="Game Over (30 Rock)">Game Over</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Florida_(30_Rock)" title="Florida (30 Rock)">Florida</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>"</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooter_Burger_.28James_Riley.29">Cooter Burger (James Riley)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Cooter Burger (James Riley)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Cooter Burger</b> (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_Broderick" title="Matthew Broderick">Matthew Broderick</a>) is a government employee and political lobbyist. He first met Jack in the declining <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush administration</a> where together they worked to get fired by developing a "Gay Bomb". Years later, Cooter works as a Republican political lobbyist and tries to persuade Jack to have <i>TGS</i> make more sketches about <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a>'s fictional new running mate, Governor Dunston. Cooter's real name is James Riley; "Cooter Burger" is a combination of two nicknames given to him by <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>.</p>
<p><i>Appears In:</i> "<a href="/wiki/Cooter_(30_Rock)" title="Cooter (30 Rock)">Cooter</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Governor_Dunston" title="Governor Dunston">Governor Dunston</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Simon_Barrons">Simon Barrons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Simon Barrons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Simon Barrons</b> (<a href="/wiki/Josh_Fadem" title="Josh Fadem">Josh Fadem</a>) is Liz's young, meek, enfeebled, low-level <a href="/wiki/Talent_agent" title="Talent agent">talent agent</a>, who usually dresses in a comically oversized suit. He mostly represents animals (bragging at one point about how one of his clients inspired a character on the show <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wonder_Pets" title="The Wonder Pets">The Wonder Pets</a></i>) and proves to be completely useless in helping Liz plan for her post-<i>TGS</i> career. Liz eventually and rightly fires him, and his efforts to get re-hired are unsuccessful, as are his efforts to finally pass the New York bar exam.</p>
<p><i>Appears In:</i> "<a href="/wiki/The_Problem_Solvers" title="The Problem Solvers">The Problem Solvers</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(30_Rock)" title="Plan B (30 Rock)">Plan B</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Today_You_Are_a_Man" title="Today You Are a Man">Today You Are a Man</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Donald">Donald</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Donald">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Donald</b> (Michael Benjamin Washington) is an entrepreneur who pretends to be Tracy Jordan's son (despite being two years older than Tracy). His money-making ideas consist of questionable business practices, such as picking out corporate names already in use (a frozen-yogurt and microbrewery restaurant called <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, and a phone service for nationwide air-quality updates called <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>). Tracy knows Donald is not his son; he supports his misguided ideas anyway, and Jack (who had convinced Tracy to cut Donald off) later tells Tracy to keep being a dad. Donald opens a <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a> dojo named for Tracy, but the business fails. He also tries to solicit Jack for an investment in a new restaurant.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a href="/wiki/Mamma_Mia_(30_Rock)" title="Mamma Mia (30 Rock)">Mamma Mia</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Chain_Reaction_of_Mental_Anguish" title="Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish">Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lynn_Onkman">Lynn Onkman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Lynn Onkman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Lynn Onkman</b> (<a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>) is Frank's girlfriend and former high school teacher. Lynn seduced Frank when he was 14 years old and they became lovers. Lynn was eventually arrested and sent to jail. Lynn was released years later and reunited with Frank on an episode of Angie's reality show "<i>Queen of Jordan</i>". Lynn and Frank broke up after an argument in which Lynn said that Frank still hadn't grown up, however, Lynn and Frank made up and continued their relationship. Frank's mother Sylvia heavily disapproved of Frank and Lynn's relationship, causing them to break up again. Liz was able to convince Sylvia to approve of Frank and Lynn's relationship when Sylvia sees Lynn's passion towards Frank, and so the two of them got back together. Despite Liz's help with Lynn and Frank's relationship, Lynn hates Liz, and has said that she believes Liz is a "terrible person". Lynn is also part of a <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexican</a> prison gang named Los Tiburones.</p>
<p><i>Appears In</i>: "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan" title="Queen of Jordan">Queen of Jordan</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Alexis_Goodlooking_and_the_Case_of_the_Missing_Whisky" title="Alexis Goodlooking and the Case of the Missing Whisky">Alexis Goodlooking and the Case of the Missing Whisky</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_characters">Minor characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Minor characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a supplementary list of recurring characters‚Äîincluding those appearing briefly in multiple episodes, such as a regularly-appearing writer‚Äîabout whom little is known.</p>
<div>
<ul>
<li><b>Gabe Person</b> (Seth Baird) - Replaces Jonathan as Jack's assistant during season 6 and several episodes of season 7. His most prominent appearance is in "<a href="/wiki/Grandmentor" title="Grandmentor">Grandmentor</a>", where he is dismissed by Jack as being nothing more than a "featured extra with no lines" after attempting to gain the lead role in the film <i>Kidnapped by Danger</i>.</li>
<li><b>Lee</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Broecker" title="Tom Broecker">Tom Broecker</a>) - The show's costume manager; appears in eleven episodes. Broecker is the real-world costume designer for <i>30 Rock</i>.</li>
<li><b>Stage manager</b> (<a href="/wiki/Teddy_Coluca" title="Teddy Coluca">Teddy Coluca</a>) - Appears in six episodes.</li>
<li><b>Tracy Davids</b> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tracy_Davids&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tracy Davids (page does not exist)">Tracy Davids</a>) - The stage manager's assistant; appears in two episodes. He yells at her<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2016)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> when she can not move quick enough ("stage manager").</li>
<li><b>D'Fwan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tituss_Burgess" title="Tituss Burgess">Tituss Burgess</a>) - A flamboyantly gay member of Angie Jordan's entourage. Appears in four episodes.</li>
<li><b>Rachel Baze</b> (Rachel Hamilton) - One of the writers on the show; in "<a href="/wiki/The_Aftermath_(30_Rock)" title="The Aftermath (30 Rock)">The Aftermath</a>", Jack mentions her last name and that she just became engaged. She has speaking parts in two episodes. She appears often in the writers room during the first two seasons, but disappears after season 2.</li>
<li><b>Anthony</b> (Anthony Atamanuik) - One of the writers on the show; speaks in the final show.</li>
<li><b>Donald</b> (<a href="/wiki/Donald_Glover" title="Donald Glover">Donald Glover</a>) - A stagehand on the show; has a speaking part in two episodes. Glover, a writer for <i>30 Rock,</i> also briefly appears as a gay student graduating from Tracy Jordan's alma mater Frank Lucas High School when Jordan gives a commencement address in "<a href="/wiki/Kidney_Now!" title="Kidney Now!">Kidney Now!</a>"</li>
<li><b>Matt</b> (Matt Dickinson) - Jack's assistant in two season-one episodes and one season-three episode (in place of Jonathan)</li>
<li><b>Stage manager</b> (<a href="/wiki/Brendan_Walsh" title="Brendan Walsh">Brendan Walsh</a>) - Shouts "Shut it down!" at the end of each of the two episodes he appears in (referred to in credits as "Shut It Down").</li>
</ul>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li><b>Alfonso Mysterioso/TGS Piano Player</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jeff_Richmond" title="Jeff Richmond">Jeff Richmond</a>) - Jenna's pianist. He appears in "<a href="/wiki/Ludachristmas" title="Ludachristmas">Ludachristmas</a>" and "Christmas Special". Richmond also appeared in "<a href="/wiki/The_Aftermath_(30_Rock)" title="The Aftermath (30 Rock)">The Aftermath</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Valentine%27s_Day" title="St. Valentine's Day">St. Valentine's Day</a>." He also appears as the <i>TGS</i> piano player in the first-season episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Baby_Show" title="The Baby Show">The Baby Show</a>". Richmond is the real-world primary composer on <i>30 Rock</i> and Tina Fey's husband. His last name is called out when he is fired from Jenna's talent show (<a href="/wiki/Hey,_Baby,_What%27s_Wrong" title="Hey, Baby, What's Wrong">Hey, Baby, What's Wrong</a>).</li>
<li><b>Richard Esposito</b> (Himself) - Jenna's hairstylist. He is long-suffering at the hands of Jenna's antics. They have an antagonistic relationship.</li>
<li><b>Tim Grandy</b> - One of the writers on the show; in "<a href="/wiki/The_Aftermath_(30_Rock)" title="The Aftermath (30 Rock)">The Aftermath</a>", Jack mentions he is from <a href="/wiki/Bowie,_Maryland" title="Bowie, Maryland">Bowie, Maryland</a>. He has a brief speaking part in "<a href="/wiki/The_C_Word" title="The C Word">The C Word</a>".</li>
<li><b>Grace Park</b> (<a href="/wiki/Charlyne_Yi" title="Charlyne Yi">Charlyne Yi</a>) - An NBC page who has a slight romantic history with Kenneth. Appeared in "<a href="/wiki/The_C_Word" title="The C Word">The C Word</a>".</li>
<li><b>Hannibal</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hannibal_Buress" title="Hannibal Buress">Hannibal Buress</a>) - A homeless man who seems to appear at moments most inconvenient to Liz and her staff. Buress was a real-life writer for <i>30 Rock</i> in seasons 5-6. He appears in "<a href="/wiki/Chain_Reaction_of_Mental_Anguish" title="Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish">Chain Reaction of Mental Anguish</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Righteous_Cowboy_Lightning" title="Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning">Operation Righteous Cowboy Lightning</a>", "<a href="/wiki/TGS_Hates_Women" title="TGS Hates Women">TGS Hates Women</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(30_Rock)" title="Plan B (30 Rock)">Plan B</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Respawn_(30_Rock)" title="Respawn (30 Rock)">Respawn</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Tuxedo_Begins" title="The Tuxedo Begins">The Tuxedo Begins</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Leap_Day_(30_Rock)" title="Leap Day (30 Rock)">Leap Day</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Jordan_2:_Mystery_of_the_Phantom_Pooper" title="Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper">Queen of Jordan 2: Mystery of the Phantom Pooper</a>".</li>
<li><b>Moonvest</b> (<a href="/wiki/Radio_Man" title="Radio Man">Craig Castaldo</a>) - A homeless man who wears a vest with crescent moons on it. He appears in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Head_and_the_Hair_(30_Rock)" title="The Head and the Hair (30 Rock)">The Head and the Hair</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Audition_Day" title="Audition Day">Audition Day</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/I_Do_Do" title="I Do Do">I Do Do</a>". His name is a reference to <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Moonves" title="Leslie Moonves">Leslie Moonves</a> (president of NBC's competitor <a href="/wiki/CBS_Corporation" title="CBS Corporation">CBS Corporation</a>) to whom the NBC executives assume Kenneth is referring, and avant-garde street musician <a href="/wiki/Moondog" title="Moondog">Moondog</a>.</li>
<li><b>Sketch-Tron 6000</b> A recurring TGS robot sketch character originally from outer space, he appears in skits like "The Bear and Robot Talk Show", flashback dreams by Tracy Jordan, vice presidential debate skits, as well as simple background appearances behind major characters or on stage for TGS rehearsals in 9 episodes over the show's 7 seasons. He appears in "<a href="/wiki/Blind_Date_(30_Rock)" title="Blind Date (30 Rock)">Blind Date</a>", <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Episode_210_(30_Rock)" title="Episode 210 (30 Rock)">Episode 210</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Cutbacks_(30_Rock)" title="Cutbacks (30 Rock)">Cutbacks</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Show" title="Live Show">Live Show</a>", "<a href="/wiki/%C2%A1Qu%C3%A9_Sorpresa!" title="¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!">¬°Qu√© Sorpresa!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Beginning_of_the_End_(30_Rock)" title="The Beginning of the End (30 Rock)">The Beginning of the End</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Governor_Dunston" title="Governor Dunston">Governor Dunston</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/A_Goon%27s_Deed_in_a_Weary_World" title="A Goon's Deed in a Weary World">A Goon's Deed in a Weary World</a>". A Sketch-Tron 6000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> fan site shows all appearances he made on the show.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Brian_Williams" title="Brian Williams">Brian Williams</a></b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himself" title="Himself">Himself</a>) - He has made a number of cameo appearances as (an exaggerated) version of himself, portrayed as clueless and trying too hard to be funny. He also appeared as <a href="/wiki/David_Brinkley" title="David Brinkley">David Brinkley</a> in the West Coast broadcast of "<a href="/wiki/Live_from_Studio_6H" title="Live from Studio 6H">Live from Studio 6H</a>".</li>
<li><b>Sherry</b> (<a href="/wiki/Adriane_Lenox" title="Adriane Lenox">Adriane Lenox</a>) - Liddy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinidadian" title="Trinidadian">Trinidadian</a> nanny who proves to be a powerful negotiator against Jack. She appears in "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Never_Too_Late_for_Now" title="It's Never Too Late for Now">It's Never Too Late for Now</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Everything_Sunny_All_the_Time_Always" title="Everything Sunny All the Time Always">Everything Sunny All the Time Always</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respawn" title="Respawn">Respawn</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leap_Day" title="Leap Day">Leap Day</a>".</li>
<li><b>Male Newscaster</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Dickson" title="Jonathan Dickson">Jonathan Dickson</a>) - The guy Tina Fey (Liz Lemon) gets her news from when she's down South and sick in bed. He appears in <a href="/wiki/Stone_Mountain_(30_Rock)" title="Stone Mountain (30 Rock)">Stone Mountain</a></li>
<li><b>Thomas Roberts</b> (Himself) - He has appeared in a number of episodes as a fictional version of himself.</li>
</ul>
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Guest_characters">Guest characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_30_Rock_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Guest characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>30 Rock</i> has featured a number of guest appearances (including cameos and featured fictional roles):</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clay_Aiken" title="Clay Aiken">Clay Aiken</a> as himself; revealed to be the cousin of Kenneth Parcell.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">Buzz Aldrin</a> as himself (former lover of Liz's mother, Margaret Lemon (then Freeman), to whom she "repeatedly lost her virginity" while Waldo, the town pervert, watched from the bushes)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Anderson" title="Harry Anderson">Harry Anderson</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Aniston" title="Jennifer Aniston">Jennifer Aniston</a> as Claire Harper (a wild college friend of Jenna and Liz)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_Armisen" title="Fred Armisen">Fred Armisen</a> as Raheem Haddad (Liz's new neighbor, whom she believes is a terrorist)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Baldwin" title="William Baldwin">William Baldwin</a> as Lance Drake Mandrell, an actor who portrays Jack in the television movie "Kidnapped by Danger".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sara_Bareilles" title="Sara Bareilles">Sara Bareilles</a> as herself</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Beastie_Boys" title="Beastie Boys">Beastie Boys</a> as themselves</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joy_Behar" title="Joy Behar">Joy Behar</a> as herself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Belzer" title="Richard Belzer">Richard Belzer</a> as himself portraying Sergeant <a href="/wiki/John_Munch" title="John Munch">John Munch</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> as herself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nick_Cannon" title="Nick Cannon">Nick Cannon</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Carrey" title="Jim Carrey">Jim Carrey</a> as himself portraying the lead in <i>Leap Dave Williams</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Carville" title="James Carville">James Carville</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Don_Cheadle" title="Don Cheadle">Don Cheadle</a> as himself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anna_Chlumsky" title="Anna Chlumsky">Anna Chlumsky</a> as Liz Lemler, Floyd's former girlfriend.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Cho" title="John Cho">John Cho</a> as Lorne, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crystal_meth" title="Crystal meth">crystal meth</a> smuggler</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_Cho" title="Margaret Cho">Margaret Cho</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kim_Jong_Il" title="Kim Jong Il">Kim Jong Il</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kim_Jong_Un" title="Kim Jong Un">Kim Jong Un</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Cole" title="Gary Cole">Gary Cole</a> as Roger</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tim_Conway" title="Tim Conway">Tim Conway</a> as Bucky Bright (an idol of Kenneth's who turns out to be a prejudiced, bisexual, womanizer); he points himself (Conway) out in a <i><a href="/wiki/McHale%27s_Navy" title="McHale's Navy">McHale's Navy</a></i> publicity photo). Tim Conway won an Emmy for the episode.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elvis_Costello" title="Elvis Costello">Elvis Costello</a> as himself</li>
